known, to be cited. In the event the owner of the dog is cited, the animal
control officer is not required to impound the dog. If the owner of the dog
running at large is not known, the dog shall in all cases be impounded. (Ord.
475, 3-7-2005)
5-1A-3: NUISANCES AND OFFENSES:
   A.   Nuisances Declared:
      1.   Noise: It is unlawful for any animal owner to allow a dog or other
animal to unreasonably disturb others by frequently barking, yelping, howling
or making other noises or disturbing the peace of other citizens. The continual
noise of the dog shall not be unreasonably audible off the property where the
dog is kept nor shall it be of such consistency and volume or at such time as
to be likely to annoy a reasonable person on the adjoining property or
elsewhere in the city.
      2.   Endangerment: It is unlawful for any animal owner to allow a dog to
unreasonably annoy, injure or endanger the safety, health, comfort or repose of
the citizens of Priest River.
      3.   Odors: It is unlawful for any animal owner to allow an animal to
create directly or indirectly any unreasonably nauseous, foul or offensive or
putrid smell.
      4.   Females In Heat: Each female dog, when in heat, shall be penned or
enclosed in such a manner as to preclude other dogs from attacking or being
attracted to such female dog in such a manner so as to create a public
nuisance.
   B.   Offenses:
      1.   Frighten Persons: It is unlawful for an animal owner to allow an
animal to render, in any way, any citizen of the city, or other person,
unreasonably insecure in life, limb or use of property.
      2.   Obstruct Passageways: It is unlawful for any animal owner to allow
an animal to unlawfully interfere with, obstruct or tend to obstruct or render
dangerous any passage a public park, street, sidewalk, alley, highway or other
public area.
      3.   Unsafe Keeping: It is unlawful for any animal owner to cage, house,
corral, fence in or maintain in any manner any animals in such numbers, crowded
conditions or other conditions as to unreasonably injure or endanger the
safety, health, comfort or life of any animal, person or property. The animal
control officer, at his discretion, may immediately release such animal.
      4.   Abandonment: It is unlawful for any person to wilfully abandon or
turn loose to run at large any animal unfit for use by reason of disease, old
age, injury or other reason. It will be the discretion of the animal control
officer to remove the animal from the premises after a twenty four (24) hour
warning notice to contact animal control is not complied with. This is in
accordance with keeping the animal safe, healthy and free of injury. Whenever
any such animal is taken for impounding, which is, in the opinion of a licensed
veterinarian, deemed unfit by reason of age, disease or injury for further use
or dangerous to be kept impounded, the animal control officer shall, within
seventy two (72) hours thereafter, cause the animal to be euthanized.
      5.   Quartering: It is unlawful to quarter animals that are natural
enemies or are otherwise incompatible together or so near each other as to
cause injury, fear or torment. All animals shall be supplied with sufficient
good food and water as often as the feeding habits of the respective animals
require, but not less than two (2) times every twenty four (24) hours for
adults. All animals and animal enclosures shall be maintained in a clean and
sanitary manner and in a state of good repair to protect the animals from
injury. (Ord. 475, 3-7-2005)
5-1A-4: DOG BITES; RABIES PROTECTION:
   A.   Biting Animals: Any person owning, possessing or harboring any animal
that bites any person or any person bitten by such animal shall report the same
to the animal control officer who shall notify the county health officer. The
animal control officer shall notify the owner of the state quarantine
requirements. If the bite does not break the skin, the dog is considered
potentially dangerous. If the skin is broken, the dog is considered dangerous
and quarantine is required.
   B.   Rabid Animals: If an animal is believed to have rabies or has been
bitten by an animal suspected of having rabies, or does not have a current
rabies vaccination and has bitten a person, such animal shall be confined to a
veterinary hospital, or appropriate animal pound or other suitable enclosure as
may be provided by the animal control officer for a period of ten (10)
consecutive calendar days or as otherwise required by law for observation. It
shall be the duty of the animal control officer or his designee to confine the
animal as required by this article. All such costs shall be at the owner's
expense. The owner shall notify the animal control officer of the fact that his
animal has been exposed to rabies.
   C.   Rabies Vaccination Required; Tag: It is unlawful for the owner of any
dog to keep or maintain such dog unless it has been vaccinated against rabies
by a licensed veterinarian. The veterinarian administering the vaccine shall
issue to the owner a certificate stating the date of vaccination and the date
of expiration, which shall be in compliance with the manufacturer's
recommendations. All dogs kept, harbored or maintained by their owners in
either yearly or every three (3) years, but it shall be in accordance with the
manufacturer's guidelines. The certificate of vaccination shall be presented at
the time of the application for a dog license. (Ord. 475, 3-7-2005)
5-1A-5: IMPOUNDMENT PROCEDURES:
The mayor or his designee is authorized and empowered to secure and maintain a
suitable pound for the purpose of carrying out the provisions of this article.
   A.   Impoundment Authorized:
      1.   It shall be the duty of every the animal control officer to
apprehend any dog found running at large or unlicensed, contrary to the
provisions of this article, and to impound such dogs in the city pound or other
suitable place; provided, that if any fierce, dangerous or vicious dog found
running at large cannot be safely taken up and impounded, such may be slain by
any peace officer.
      2.   The animal control officer so impounding any dog shall record a
description of the dog, and whether licensed, in a book kept for that purpose.
If the dog is licensed and is wearing a license tag when apprehended, the
animal control officer shall also record the name and address of the owner and
the number of the tag.
   B.   Holding Period; Disposition:
      1.   It shall be duty of the animal control officer to keep all animals
so impounded for a period of three (3) days after the posting and mailing of
such notice. If the dog has not been redeemed by the owner, it may be
destroyed, or sold for a sum of money sufficient to discharge the costs and
charges incurred by the city for impounding and keeping the dog, together with
the license fee for the current year if unpaid. No dog, which appears to be
suffering from rabies, or any dog of fierce, dangerous or vicious propensities
shall be released from the pound, but shall be destroyed.
      2.   The buyer of any dog under the provisions of this section shall
become the owner of the dog, free from any claim or title of the original owner
or harborer.
   C.   Notice To Owner; Fees: Not later than one day after the impounding of
any dog, the animal control officer, or his designee, shall cause a written
notice of such impounding to be posted in a conspicuous place in the office of
the city clerk. Such notice shall be kept posted for a period of three (3)
days. If the dog is wearing a license tag when apprehended, the animal control
officer shall cause a copy of the notice to be mailed to the address shown on
the application for license. The owner of any dog so impounded may reclaim such
dog upon the payment of license fee, if unpaid, and all of the costs and
charges incurred by the city for impounding and keeping costs and charges. If
an owner of a dog is notified that the city is in possession of their dog and
the owner fails to claim the dog within three (3) days, keeping charges and a
disposal fee will be charged. Pound fees, fees for an animal impounded,
disposal charges and fees for notification of the owner of an animal impounded
will be set by resolution and reviewed on a regular basis. (Ord. 475, 3-7-2005)
5-1A-6: ABATEMENT AND ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Upon the first or any subsequent complaint, or upon the discovery of an
animal nuisance, the animal control officer of the city may order the owner of
the animal, or other person creating, keeping, maintaining or permitting, the
same to abate it, and in default thereof to undertake the abatement on behalf
of the city. At least ten (10) days before he commences abatement, save in
cases of immediate necessity, the officer shall notify the person creating,
keeping, maintaining or permitting the nuisance, the animal owner and any
person in possession of the animal, if known, of his intentions, and the notice
shall be served personally or by first class mail and shall describe with
particularity the nature of the violation of the sections of this code or other
law which is being violated and specifying a reasonable time within which the
abatement must be accomplished.
   B.   The order may be appealed by filing a written notice of appeal with the
mayor or the city clerk within two (2) business days of the order having been
served. The appeal will be heard at the next regular city council meeting by
the city council who shall, after hearing, make findings, and enter an order
either affirming, repealing or changing the order.
   C.   In addition to such other penalties as may be imposed, a court entering
a judgment of guilty to a charge of creating an animal nuisance may order the
abatement of the same on such terms and conditions as may be just and
equitable.
   D.   By way of additional or alternate enforcement, it shall be a violation
of this article for an animal owner to allow the barking, yelping, howling or
other noise caused by the animal if the noises are unreasonable or frequently
and habitually occur at unreasonable periods of times of the day or continue
for unreasonable periods of time. Law enforcement of the city may issue a
criminal citation to the animal owner under this article upon any occurrence.
(Ord. 475, 3-7-2005)
5-1A-7: VIOLATIONS; PENALTY:
   A.   Except as otherwise noted, any person violating any of the provisions
of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof
shall be fined as provided in the general penalty in section
1-4-1 of this code. However, the city's prosecuting attorney may elect to
refrain from initiating criminal prosecution on the violation if the violator
pays to the city clerk, within fifteen (15) days of receipt of the complaint of
such violation a civil assessment in the amount set forth in section
1-4-5 of this code.
(Ord. 475, 3-7-2005; amd. Ord. 631, 9-5-2023)
ARTICLE B.KENNELS AND PET SHOPS
SECTION:
5-1B-1: Definitions
5-1B-2: License Requirements
5-1B-3: Standards
5-1B-4: Primary Enclosures
5-1B-5: Feeding
5-1B-6: Enforcement
5-1B-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following definitions shall apply to the words and terms used in this
article:
KENNEL: Includes:
   A.   Commercial Kennel: An establishment primarily offering boarding,
training and/or breeding services and the associated sale of dogs, with the
exclusion of veterinary hospitals.
   B.   Noncommercial Kennel: Any one household that keeps, maintains, harbors
or possesses more than three (3) dogs over six (6) months of age. Incidental
sale of such animals shall not disqualify households from noncommercial kennel
status.
PET ANIMAL: Any domesticated or wild animal, including dogs, cats, birds, small
rodents or small nonpoisonous reptiles, which is fed, watered, harbored or
allowed by any person to remain at or in the vicinity of a residence or place
of business in the city.
PET SHOP: A retail or wholesale business primarily offering for sale pet
animals and/or pet animal products, excluding commercial kennels.
PRIMARY ENCLOSURE: A separate enclosure or cage which segregates one animal
from another animal or animals.
VETERINARY HOSPITAL: Any establishment in which the practice of veterinary
medicine is the primary business. (Ord. 475, 3-7-2005)
5-1B-2: LICENSE REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   License Required: It is unlawful for any person to operate, keep or
maintain within the city limits a kennel or pet shop without having first
obtained a license from the city and being in compliance with all provisions of
this article. The annual fee for a license, issued hereunder or any renewal
thereof, shall be established by resolution. (Ord. 475, 3-7-2005; amd. Ord.
492, 2-12-2006)
   B.   Application For License: Any person applying for a license or renewal
thereof under this article shall file with the city clerk an application on a
form prescribed by the city clerk, accompanied by the annual license fee.
   C.   Procedure For Licensing: No license or renewal thereof shall be issued
hereunder until:
      1.   There has been an inspection by an animal control officer of the
premises being licensed and a determination by him that all requirements of
this article will be met;
      2.   There is an adequate means of restraining animals from running at
large or disturbing the peace;
      3.   The proposed facilities are located in an applicable zone under the
zoning regulations of the city.
   D.   Term Of License: Any license or renewal thereof issued hereunder shall
be for a calendar year or portion thereof and must be renewed each calendar
year on or before January 31. Such license shall not be assignable or
transferable either to another person or for another location.
   E.   Posting: When issued, a license shall be displayed in a manner and at a
location so as to be readily visible by the public. (Ord. 475, 3-7-2005)
5-1B-3: STANDARDS:
   A.   General Facilities: All licensed premises shall be provide the
following:
      1.   Water And Food: Adequate and potable water shall be available at all
times to pet animals kept longer than twenty four (24) hours unless veterinary
orders indicate to the contrary. Watering and feeding receptacles shall be
cleaned at least once daily.
      2.   Storage: Supplies of food and bedding shall be stored and adequately
protected against infestation or contamination by vermin. Refrigeration shall
be provided for perishable food.
      3.   Waste Disposal: Provisions shall be made for the removal and
disposal of animal and food wastes, bedding, dead animals and debris. Disposal
facilities shall also be provided and operated as to minimize vermin
infestation, odors and disease hazards.
      4.   Washrooms And Sinks: Facilities such as washrooms, basins or sinks
shall be provided to maintain cleanliness among caretakers.
      5.   Communicable Disease: Animals with potential communicable diseases
shall be housed in separate rooms from healthy boarding animals.
   B.   Indoor Facilities: In addition to the requirements of subsection A of
this section, indoor facilities licensed hereunder shall provide the following:
      1.   Ventilation: Indoor housing for pet animals shall be adequately
ventilated to provide for health and comfort of the animals at all times. They
shall be provided with fresh air, either by means of windows, doors, vents or
air conditioning, and shall be ventilated so as to minimize drafts, odors and
moisture condensation. Auxiliary ventilation such as exhaust fans and vents or
air conditioning shall be provided when the ambient temperature is eighty five
degrees Fahrenheit (85°F) or higher unless the ambient temperature requirements
of the specific species differ.
      2.   Lighting: Indoor housing for pet animals shall have ample artificial
light which is of good quality and is well distributed. Such lighting shall
provide uniformly distributed illumination of sufficient intensity to permit
routine inspection and cleaning during the entire working period.
      3.   Interior Surfaces: The interior building surfaces of indoor housing
facilities and dog houses shall be constructed and maintained so that they are
impervious to moisture and may be readily cleaned.
      4.   Drainage: A suitable method shall be provided to rapidly eliminate
excess water from indoor housing facilities. If drains are used, they shall be
properly constructed and kept in good repair to avoid foul odors therefrom. If
closed drainage systems are used, they shall be equipped with traps and so
installed as to prevent any backup of sewage and odors.
      5.   Dogs Four Months Or Older: Dogs four (4) months or older which are
housed longer than a twenty four (24) hour period shall be provided with
adequate, separate, cleanable cages and shall be permitted exercise periods at
least twice each day for a minimum of five (5) minutes each period unless an
exercise run is provided. Such an exercise run must have an area of twenty (20)
square feet for a dog of thirty (30) pounds or less, and a minimum of thirty
six (36) square feet for dogs over thirty (30) pounds.
   C.   Outdoor Facilities: In addition to the standards required under
subsection A of this section, outdoor facilities licensed hereunder shall
provide the following:
      1.   Shelter:
         a.   Sunlight: When sunlight is likely to cause overheating or
discomfort, sufficient shade shall be provided to allow all pet animals kept
outdoors to protect themselves from the direct rays of the sun.
         b.   Rain Or Snow: Pet animals kept outdoors shall be provided with
access to shelter to allow them to remain dry during rain or snow.
         c.   Cold Weather: Shelter shall be provided for all pet animals kept
outdoors when the atmospheric temperature falls below fifty degrees Fahrenheit
(50°F). Sufficient clean bedding material or other means of protection from the
weather elements shall be provided with the ambient temperature falls below
that temperature to which the animal is acclimated.
      2.   Drainage: A suitable method shall be provided to rapidly eliminate
excess water.
      3.   Dogs Four Months Or Older: Dogs four (4) months or older which are
housed longer than a twenty four (24) period shall be provided with separate,
adequate, cleanable enclosures and shall be permitted exercise periods at least
twice a day for a minimum of five (5) minutes each period unless an exercise
run is provided. Such an exercise run must have an area of twenty (20) square
feet for a dog of thirty (30) pounds or less, and minimum of thirty six (36)
square feet for dogs over thirty (30) pounds.
      4.   Individual Cages: Individual cages shall not be required for
noncommercial kennels. (Ord. 475, 3-7-2005)
5-1B-4: PRIMARY ENCLOSURES:
   A.   General: Primary enclosures shall:
      1.   Not be required for noncommercial kennels;
      2.   Be structurally sound and maintained in good repair to protect the
animals from injury, to contain them and to keep predators out. They shall be
constructed of a material that is easily cleanable and maintained so as to
enable the pet animals to remain dry and clean and provide convenient access to
clean food and water;
      3.   Be constructed and maintained so as to provide sufficient space to
allow each pet animal to turn about freely and to easily stand, sit and lie in
a comfortable, normal position;
      4.   For each animal housed therein, be provided a minimum square footage
of floor space equal to the mathematical square of the sum of the length of the
animal in inches, as measured from the tip of its nose to the base of its tail,
plus six inches (6"), expressed in square feet. This requirement may be
computed using the following equation: (length of animal in inches plus 6)
times (length of animal in inches plus 6) equals required area in square inches
(divided by 144) equals required square feet of floor space.
      5.   The height of any outdoor kennel shall be at least six feet (6');
      6.   Be used for housing not more than one animal unless requested by the
owners of each animal housed therein;
      7.   Subsections A3 and A4 of this section shall not apply to animals
being housed for medical or grooming purposes or for less than seventy two (72)
hours.
   B.   Sanitation:
      1.   Excreta shall be removed from primary enclosures as often as
necessary to prevent contamination of the pet animals contained therein and to
reduce disease, hazards and odors. When a hosing or flushing method is used for
cleaning a cage, the pet animals shall be removed during the cleaning process
and adequate measures shall be taken to protect the animals in other enclosures
from being contaminated with water and other wastes.
      2.   Cages, rooms, hard surfaced pens and runs shall be cleaned by
washing all soiled surfaces with a safe and effective disinfectant.
      3.   Pens and runs using gravel, sand or dirt shall be sanitized by
removing the soiled gravel, sand or dirt and replacing it as necessary.
      4.   An effective program for the control of insects, ectoparasite, avian
and mammalian pests shall be established and maintained where indicated. (Ord.
475, 3-7-2005)
5-1B-5: FEEDING:
   A.   Pet animals which are housed for more than twenty four (24) hours shall
be fed at least once a day except as otherwise might be required to provide
adequate veterinary care. The food shall be free from contamination, wholesome,
palatable and of sufficient quality and nutritive value to meet the normal
daily requirements for the condition and size of the animal.
   B.   Food receptacles shall be accessible to the pet animal and shall be
located so as to minimize contamination by excreta. Feeding pans shall be
durable and kept clean. The food receptacles shall be cleaned daily. Disposal
food receptacles may be used but must be discarded after each feeding. Self-
feeders may be used for the feeding of dry food and they shall be sanitized
regularly to prevent molding, deterioration or caking of feed. (Ord. 475, 3-7-
2005)
5-1B-6: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Violation:
      1.   Any person violating any provisions of this article or who shall
hinder, impede or obstruct an enforcing officer in the performance of his duty
of enforcement, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof
fined as provided in the general penalty in section
1-4-1 of this code.
      2.   The animal control officer is the officer responsible for the
enforcement of this article and shall have the authority and duty to enter any
licensed premises at any reasonable hour to inspect the same.
   B.   Revocation, Denial Of License:
      1.   The city council shall have the right to revoke any license once
granted or deny annual renewal thereof when it appears that any operator or
licensee has violated any of the provisions of this article or any ordinance of
the city, the state or the United States involving cruelty or mistreatment of
animals. Prior to the revocation of any license or the denial of an application
of a renewal thereof, written notice of the reason for such action shall be
given to the applicant or licensee by the city clerk. Such notice shall state
that the applicant or licensee may request a hearing on such decision by the
city council within ten (10) days of receiving the notice.
      2.   Should the applicant or licensee request a hearing within such ten
(10) day period, the applicant shall be notified in writing by the city clerk
of the time and place of the hearing, and the license shall not be revoked
until after a decision is made by the city council that grounds exist for such
revocation or denial.
(Ord. 475, 3-7-2005; amd. Ord. 631, 9-5-2023)
ARTICLE C.DOMESTIC FOWL
SECTION:
5-1C-1: Keeping Of Domestic Fowl
5-1C-1: KEEPING OF DOMESTIC FOWL:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any household to own, harbor, or possess
domestic fowl other than authorized by this section and in accordance with
limitations and requirements established herein.
   B.   Chickens are permitted on any single-family detached lot in the city of
Priest River. Each property is permitted a maximum of six (6) hens. Roosters
are prohibited within the city limits.
   C.   Coops and all feed supply shall be secured to prevent mice and other
pests.
   D.   Coops, hutches, or similar containment structures must be kept at least
thirty feet (30') from the front property line, five feet (5') from the side
and rear property lines, at least fifteen feet (15') from the residence on
site, and at least twenty five feet (25') from any neighboring residence.
   E.   Coops, hutches, or similar structures shall not be attached to a shared
fence.
   F.   No coop, hutch, or similar containment structure, nor any confinement
fence or pen shall be constructed or maintained over, on, or adjacent to any
septic tank or drain field.
   G.   It shall be the sole duty of the persons owning such chickens to keep
them in secure confinement sufficient to prevent them from roaming onto any
adjacent lands.
   H.   The persons owning such chickens shall keep them, and all grounds upon
or facilities within which they are housed, clean and sanitary. (Ord. 548, 6-
18-2012)
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
5-2-1: Trespassing
5-2-2: Damage To Property
5-2-3: Hazardous Fences
5-2-4: Human Powered Vehicles
5-2-5: Sports On Public Property
5-2-6: Graffiti
5-2-7: Possession Of An Open Container Of An Alcoholic Beverage In Public
Places
5-2-1: TRESPASSING:
It is unlawful for any person to take down any fence, or to let down any bars,
or to open any gate in or on the property of another without the consent of the
owner, occupant or person in charge thereof. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
5-2-2: DAMAGE TO PROPERTY:
   A.   Malicious Injury: It is unlawful for any person wilfully and
maliciously to injure, deface, mutilate, remove, pull down, break or in any
manner interfere with or molest, or secrete or destroy any real or personal
property belonging to or under the control of another.
   B.   Depositing Injurious Substances On Public Thoroughfares: It is unlawful
for any person to deposit, place or allow to remain upon any public
thoroughfare any material or substance injurious to persons or property. (Ord.
482, 6-5-2006)
5-2-3: HAZARDOUS FENCES:
   A.   Electric Fences: It is unlawful for any person to erect or maintain any
fence, where any part of the fence may be electrified, in any area of the city
except as an animal impound fence on residential property zoned for the keeping
of large animals as defined in the zoning ordinance.
   B.   Barbed Wire Or Razor Wire Fences: It is unlawful for any person to
erect or maintain any fence or any fence constructed in whole or in part of
barbed wire or razor wire except as a property guard on commercial, industrial
or municipal use zoned property or, with the approval of the public works
supervisor, as an animal impound fence on residential property zoned for the
keeping of large animals as defined in the zoning ordinance. Any person wanting
to use any barbed wire or razor wire fence used as a property guard on
commercial, industrial or municipal use zoned property that borders residential
property must submit a request to, and receive the approval of, the public
works supervisor. (Ord. 516, 10-6-2008)
5-2-4: HUMAN POWERED VEHICLES:
   A.   Definition: A "human powered vehicle" is a skateboard, roller skates,
in-line skates, scooters or other toy vehicle operated by human power excluding
perambulators or wheelchairs or other like vehicles being operated by
handicapped or infirm persons.
   B.   Riding On Public Property: Except to cross a sidewalk when entering or
exiting an alleyway, a private drive or a crosswalk, and where signs are
posted, it is unlawful to ride, operate or cause to be operated any human
powered vehicle on the sidewalks of the city.
   C.   Vehicle Demonstrations: Nothing in this chapter shall prohibit the
mayor and/or the city council from allowing bicycle, skateboard or other human
powered vehicle exhibits or demonstrations at designated locations by obtaining
a special event permit from the city. Security and porta potties are the
responsibility of the permit holder. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
5-2-5: SPORTS ON PUBLIC PROPERTY:
   A.   Sports Equipment: It is unlawful to set up, operate or use a skateboard
ramp, basketball hoop, or any other type of sports equipment on any public
property, nor within three feet (3') of each side of a paved road.
   B.   Playing Ball On Streets: It is unlawful for any person to play ball or
throw any ball to and fro upon any public thoroughfare. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
5-2-6: GRAFFITI:
   A.   Prohibited: It is hereby declared unlawful for any person to place or
put, by any means, any drawing, inscription, figure, symbol, or mark or any
type commonly known as graffiti on any public or private property without the
permission of the owner of the premises on which the surface is located, or
upon any natural surfaces such as rocks or trees, or any other surface
whatsoever.
   B.   Removal Required: Any person found to be in violation of this section
shall be required to remove or cause to be removed the graffiti from the
surface on which it was placed. Inasmuch as it is often not possible to
determine the identity of the person who applied the graffiti, it shall be the
duty of the owner or person in control of the premises on which the graffiti
has been applied to promptly remove the graffiti after notice as hereinafter
set forth. If, after notice as hereinafter provided, the graffiti nuisance is
not abated, the City shall proceed to abate the graffiti nuisance and the costs
of same shall be assessed against the property.
   C.   Notice To Remove:
      1.   Whenever the City discovers graffiti on any public or private
property or any surfaces visible to persons utilizing public rights-of-way
within the City, it shall, whenever seasonal temperatures permit the painting
of exterior surfaces, cause a notice to be issued to the owner or person in
control of the premises to remove the graffiti or cover it with paint or other
suitable substance.
      2.   Said notice shall be served upon the owner(s) of the affected
premises, as shown on the last Property Tax assessment rolls of Bonner County,
Idaho, with a copy to the occupant of the premises. If there is no known
address for the owner, the notice shall be served at the property address.
Service of the notice may be accomplished through personal service on the
owner, occupant, or person in charge or control of the property or by certified
mail.
      3.   If the City removes the graffiti under the provisions of this
section, a statement of charges billed to the property owner shall be mailed or
personally delivered to the property owner. If payment is not received from the
property owner within thirty (30) days, the amount billed shall, in accordance
with State law, be assessed as a special assessment collectible against the
subject property as other State, County and Municipal taxes. (Ord. 482, 6-5-
2006)
5-2-7: POSSESSION OF AN OPEN CONTAINER OF AN ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE IN PUBLIC
PLACES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to consume any alcoholic beverage or to
have in his or her possession any open container of any alcoholic beverage in a
public place within the City of Priest River, including any street, any public
or private parking lot, or any public or private property open to the public,
except as otherwise provided by law.
Nothing herein will be interpreted to prevent residents or their guests from
consuming alcoholic beverages or having an open container of any alcohol
beverage in public areas zoned Residential. This exception does not apply to
customers of any business licensed to sell alcoholic beverages for on premises
consumption when such alcoholic beverage is taken away from the premises so
licensed or in public areas within the design review overlay historic district.
"Container of an alcoholic beverage" includes, without limitation, a bottle or
can labeled as containing such a beverage, no matter what it in fact contains,
and a container containing such a beverage no matter how labeled. An "alcoholic
beverage" is any liquid or solid containing ethyl alcohol or synthetic ethyl
alcohol in an amount of three percent (3%) or more by weight (6 proof); a
manufacturer's label on the bottle or can or on a package out of which such
container came is conclusive evidence of content.
"Open container" shall be defined as the original receptacle of the alcoholic
beverage, whose seal has been broken or cap removed, or any other container
into which the alcoholic beverage has been placed which does not have affixed
thereon a permanent airtight seal or cap. (Ord. 606, 8-5-2019)
CHAPTER 3
MINORS
SECTION:
5-3-1: Curfew
5-3-1: CURFEW:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this chapter:
   GUARDIAN: The legal guardian appointed by a court to have the control and
custody of the particular child that may be involved, or the person who may be
in the actual control and custody of such child by consent of the parents,
guardian or such minor, without court order.
   PARENT: The natural parent or stepparent of the particular child that may be
concerned.
   PUBLIC PLACE: Includes, but is not limited to, parks, playgrounds and
similar premises open to the general public.
   STREET OR HIGHWAY: Any road, alley, sidewalk, thoroughfare or other course
of travel open to the general public.
   B.   Hours Of Curfew:
      1.   It is unlawful for any child under the age of eighteen (18) years to
be in or upon, or to congregate or loiter in or upon any street, highway or
public place in the city between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and six
o'clock (6:00) A.M. on Sunday through Thursday, and between the hours of eleven
o'clock (11:00) P.M. and six o'clock (6:00) A.M. on Friday and Saturday.
      2.   The hours indicated in this section are with reference to the
standard time prevailing in the city, whether the same is Pacific Standard or
Pacific Daylight Saving Time.
   C.   Exceptions: The following described persons are excepted from the terms
of this section:
      1.   Children accompanied by their parents or guardians;
      2.   Children who have been sent by their parent or guardian on urgent
family business or errand;
      3.   Children in the course of employment or enroute to and from such
employment;
      4.   Children engaged in or going to or from activities sponsored by a
school or church;
      5.   Children engaged in or going to or from any private social affair;
provided, however, that in no event shall permission be granted for children to
attend any affair or to be going to and from such affair later than twelve
o'clock (12:00) midnight.
   D.   Parental Responsibility: It is unlawful for any parent or guardian,
wilfully or negligently, to permit a child under the age of eighteen (18) years
to violate any of the provisions of this section. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
TRAFFIC REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-1-1: Designation Of Authority
6-1-2: Local Restrictions On Certain Streets
6-1-3: Reduction Of State Imposed Speed Limits
6-1-4: Recreational Vehicles
6-1-5: Violation
6-1-1: DESIGNATION OF AUTHORITY:
Whenever in the judgment of the City Council the operation of any vehicle on
any street or alley, or any portion thereof, of the sizes and weights and at
the rates of speed permissible by law, would interfere with the safe and
efficient use of such street or alley by the traveling public, or will cause
damage to said street or alley by reason of climatic or other conditions, the
City Council shall have authority to make regulations reducing the permissible
sizes, weights or speeds of vehicles operated on such street or alley, or any
portion thereof, for such periods as may be necessary for public safety or for
the protection of such street or alley, and shall erect and maintain signs
designating such regulations at each end of such street or alley, or any
portion thereof. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
6-1-2: LOCAL RESTRICTIONS ON CERTAIN STREETS:
   A.   Weight Restrictions: It is unlawful for any person to operate any
vehicle with a gross weight in excess of the amounts specified when signs are
erected, by authority of the City Council, giving notice thereof.
   B.   Loaded Trucks Prohibited From Using Posted City Roads: When so posted
during the spring breakup, loaded trucks are prohibited from using posted City
streets. For the purposes of this section, a "truck" is defined as any vehicle
with a GVWR of twenty six thousand (26,000) pounds or greater and is licensed
with a commercial truck license plate or any vehicle that requires a commercial
driver's license to legally operate. A "loaded truck" is defined as any vehicle
with a GVWR of twenty six thousand (26,000) pounds or greater that is loaded
with any cargo for which it was designed to carry. Empty trucks shall be
allowed on posted City streets, but their speed shall be no greater than ten
(10) miles per hour. The Public Works Department may issue specific weight
exemptions for loaded trucks. Such exemptions shall be on a case by case basis
and shall not confer a continuing right to move loaded trucks on posted City
streets. Such exemptions shall be based on the expected temperature and street
conditions at the time of exemption, and such exemption shall be for weight
only and shall not exempt speed restrictions. The City Police Department shall
be notified of all such specific exemptions. Local deliveries of home heating
fuel, school supplies, critical healthcare supplies, restaurant and merchant
supplies, and public service and utility vehicles are exempt from the weight
restrictions imposed when streets are so posted but are not exempt from the
speed restrictions imposed when streets are so posted. School buses are exempt
from the weight restrictions and speed restrictions imposed when streets are so
posted when traveling on designated school bus routes.
   C.   Certain Vehicles On Heavily Traveled Streets: The City Council is
authorized to determine and designate those heavily traveled streets upon which
motor driven cycles, bicycles or other nonmotorized traffic shall be
prohibited, and shall erect appropriate signs giving notice thereof. When such
signs are so erected, it is unlawful for any person to disobey the restrictions
stated on such signs.
   D.   Special Purpose Vehicles: Special purpose vehicles, such as tow trucks,
dump trucks, truck trailers and construction equipment, are not permitted in
residential areas unless being used for their intended purpose. (Ord. 594, 3-5-
2018)
6-1-3: REDUCTION OF STATE IMPOSED SPEED LIMITS:
The City hereby enacts the provisions of Idaho Code 49-201(4) which grants
authority to duly elected officials of an incorporated city acting in their
capacity of a local authority, to establish lower speed limits for portions of
State highways, excluding controlled access and interstate highways, that pass
through residential, urban or business districts within the jurisdiction of the
incorporated city, for the purpose of enhancing motorist and pedestrian safety.
A reduction in speed limit on all State highways passing through the City to
thirty five (35) miles per hour is mandated as follows:
Beginning at all boundaries of the incorporated City accessed by State
highways, providing for a set speed limit within the City limits on all State
highways, unless otherwise posted, subject to current restrictions imposed by
local authority for such periods as may be necessary for public safety. (Ord.
482, 6-5-2006)
6-1-4: RECREATIONAL VEHICLES:
No person shall operate an ATV (all-terrain vehicle) or any other type of
recreational vehicle that is not properly licensed upon any public ways and
property within the City. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
6-1-5: VIOLATION:
Unless otherwise provided for under Idaho Motor Vehicle Laws, a violation of
any provision of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor, and shall be punishable
in the manner provided in the general penalty in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
CHAPTER 2
STOPPING, STANDING AND PARKING
SECTION:
6-2-1: Authority
6-2-2: Obstructing Roadways
6-2-3: Prohibited Parking In Designated Locations
6-2-4: Parking Restrictions
6-2-5: Handicap Parking Spaces
6-2-6: Removal Of Improperly Parked Vehicles
6-2-7: Abandoned, Stolen Or Wrecked Vehicles On Public Property
6-2-8: Violation
6-2-1: AUTHORITY:
The city council is authorized to determine and designate, by proper signs, any
street, alley, or any portion thereof, on which the stopping, standing or
parking of vehicles would create an especially hazardous condition or would
cause an unusual delay in traffic. When official signs are erected at such
hazardous or congested places, it is unlawful for any person to stop, stand or
park a vehicle in any such designated place. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
6-2-2: OBSTRUCTING ROADWAYS:
   A.   It is unlawful for any person to park any vehicle upon a street in such
a manner or under such conditions as to obstruct the normally traveled portion
of the roadway, except as provided in subsection B of this section.
   B.   It is unlawful for any person to stop, stand or park a vehicle within
the city on a roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or curb
of a street, except as provided when:
      1.   It is necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic;
      2.   It is in compliance with law or at the direction of a law
enforcement officer, a firefighter in the course of his duties, or a lawfully
established traffic control device;
      3.   It is for purposes of unloading a bona fide commercial vehicle for
the purposes of delivering goods or wares to a residence or commercial
establishment situated immediately adjacent thereto; provided, however, the
commercial vehicle exception created in this section shall not exceed a period
of fifteen (15) minutes from the time of stopping such vehicle to the time of
removing the same. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
   C.   It shall be unlawful for any person to park a vehicle within six feet
(6') of the normally traveled portion of any city street at any place within
the residential area of the city at any time after snow has fallen, and the
accumulation of snow is such that it covers said street, or in such a way as to
disrupt normal snowplowing operations. Said parking restrictions shall remain
in effect after the snow has ceased to fall and until snow removal operations
have been completed. However, this provision shall not apply to physicians on
emergency calls. (Ord. 493, 12-18-2006)
6-2-3: PROHIBITED PARKING IN DESIGNATED LOCATIONS:
   A.   General: It is unlawful for any person to stop, stand or park a
vehicle, except when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic, or in
compliance with law or the direction of a police officer or traffic control
device, in any of the following places:
      1.   On a sidewalk;
      2.   In front of a public or private driveway;
      3.   Within an intersection;
      4.   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant;
      5.   On a crosswalk;
      6.   Within twenty feet (20') of a crosswalk at an intersection;
      7.   Within thirty feet (30') upon the approach to any flashing beacon,
stop sign or traffic control signal;
      8.   Between a safety zone and the adjacent curb, or within thirty feet
(30') of points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone,
unless the chief of police has indicated a different length of a zone by signs
or markings;
      9.   Within fifty feet (50') of the nearest rail of a railroad crossing;
      10.   Within twenty feet (20') of the driveway entrance to any fire
station, and on the side of a street opposite the entrance to any fire station
within seventy five feet (75') of such entrance, when properly signposted;
      11.   Alongside of or opposite any street obstruction or excavation when
stopping, standing or parking would obstruct traffic;
      12.   On a roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or
curb of a street;
      13.   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure upon a highway, or
within a highway tunnel;
      14.   At any place where official signs prohibit stopping;
      15.   Against the direction of lawful traffic movement.
   B.   Illegal Movement: It is unlawful for any person to move a vehicle not
lawfully under his control into any such prohibited area, or away from a curb
such distance as is unlawful.
   C.   Truck Parking In Business District: Parking of sixteen thousand
(16,000) GVW or larger trucks and/or truck trailers is prohibited within the
business district of the city.
   D.   Parking For Selling Or Repairing: It is unlawful for any person to park
a vehicle upon any roadway or public thoroughfare for the principal purpose of:
      1.   Displaying such vehicle for sale;
      2.   Greasing or repairing such vehicle, except repairs necessitated by
an emergency. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
6-2-4: PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   School Areas: The city council is authorized to erect signs indicating
no parking upon either or both sides of any street adjacent to any school
property when such parking would interfere with traffic or create a hazardous
situation. When official signs are erected indicating no parking is allowed
upon either or both sides of a street adjacent to any school property, as
authorized in this subsection, it is unlawful for any person to park a vehicle
in any such designated place.
   B.   Narrow Streets: The city council is authorized to erect signs
indicating no parking upon any street when the width of the roadway does not
exceed twenty feet (20'). When official signs prohibiting parking are erected
upon narrow streets, as authorized in this subsection, it is unlawful for any
person to park a vehicle upon any such street in violation of any such signs.
   C.   Alleys: It is unlawful for any person to park a vehicle within an alley
in such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten
feet (10') of the width of the roadway for the free movement of vehicular
traffic, and it is unlawful for a person to stop, stand or park a vehicle
within an alley in such a position as to block the driveway entrance to any
abutting property. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
   D.   All Night Parking: It is unlawful for any person to park a vehicle on
the following streets within the business district for a period of time longer
than fifteen (15) minutes between the hours of three o'clock (3:00) A.M. and
six o'clock (6:00) A.M. of any day, except for law enforcement or fire
department personnel performing their lawful duties and physicians on emergency
calls:
      1.   High Street between Church Street and Treat Street;
      2.   Main Street from Albeni Road to Montgomery Street. (Ord. 493, 12-18-
2006)
6-2-5: HANDICAP PARKING SPACES:
   A.   Parking Restrictions: It is unlawful for the driver of a vehicle to
park such vehicle in a parking space designated by sign or marking as reserved
for the handicapped unless such vehicle has then displayed upon it the special
license plate, or the special card pursuant to Idaho Code 49-410. Such
specially designated spaces shall conform to the requirements of Idaho Code 49-
213.
   B.   Penalty: The penalty for a violation of this section shall be the sum
of fifty dollars ($50.00), which shall be paid within seven (7) days of the
violation. If such sum is not paid within seven (7) days, the penalty shall be
the sum of one hundred dollars ($100.00) if paid within fourteen (14) days of
such violation. If such sum is not paid within fourteen (14) days, the penalty
shall be the sum of one hundred forty one dollars and fifty cents ($141.50).
(Ord. 482, 6-5-2006; amd. Ord. 631, 9-5-2023)
6-2-6: REMOVAL OF IMPROPERLY PARKED VEHICLES:
   A.   Any vehicle parked in violation of traffic regulations, or any vehicle
parked so as to obstruct the free movement of traffic or causing a traffic
hazard, may be removed upon order of the city law enforcement agency. Any such
vehicle so removed shall be kept under the control of the city law enforcement
agency until the owner or their authorized agent pays the reasonable cost of
removal and storage in addition to the penalty provided for such improper
parking.
   B.   Any such vehicle shall be deemed to be improperly parked after a period
of fifteen (15) minutes.
   C.   The cost of redemption shall include the actual cost and expense of the
removal in addition to a reasonable per day storage charge and such costs and
expenses shall be a lien in favor of the city. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
6-2-7: ABANDONED, STOLEN OR WRECKED VEHICLES ON PUBLIC PROPERTY:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section:
   ABANDONED MOTOR VEHICLE OR OTHER PERSONAL PROPERTY: An automobile or
personal property which remains upon the street or other public property for a
period of time longer than forty eight (48) hours, the owner of which cannot be
located or the owner of which refuses to remove the same.
   B.   Removal; Costs: The city law enforcement agency is hereby authorized,
in addition to any penalty that may be provided therefor, to remove an
unidentified, stolen, wrecked or abandoned motor vehicle or other personal
property found upon any public thoroughfare or other property of the city, and
shall keep the same in its custody and control at such place as may be
designated by the city law enforcement agency until redeemed by the owner. All
such unidentified, stolen, wrecked or abandoned motor vehicles or other
personal property which now is in the possession of the city law enforcement
agency shall be subject to the actual cost of removal or tow in from the public
place, and a reasonable per day storage charge, for as long as the same is in
possession and custody.
   C.   Abandoning Vehicles Prohibited: It is unlawful for any owner or any
person in charge of a motor vehicle or other personal property to abandon the
same upon the street or public places of the city. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
6-2-8: VIOLATION:
Unless otherwise provided for under Idaho motor vehicle laws, a violation of
any provision of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor and shall be punished as
provided in the general penalty in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
CHAPTER 3
SPEED LIMIT REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-3-1: Purpose
6-3-2: Speed Limits
6-3-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to adopt uniform traffic speed limits within the
city of Priest River. (Ord. 489, 9-18-2006)
6-3-2: SPEED LIMITS:
   A.   Streets: The uniform speed limit on all streets within the city of
Priest River shall be twenty five (25) miles per hour except as otherwise
legally posted.
   B.   Alleyways: The uniform speed limit for all alleyways within the city of
Priest River shall be ten (10) miles per hour.
   C.   School Zones: The uniform speed limit for all identified school zones
when children are present shall be fifteen (15) miles per hour except as
otherwise legally posted. (Ord. 489, 9-18-2006)
CHAPTER 4
VEHICLE SOUNDS
SECTION:
6-4-1: Air Compression Brakes
6-4-2: Violation
6-4-1: AIR COMPRESSION BRAKES:
The use of air compression brakes (also known as "jake brakes") by motor
vehicles within the city limits of the city of Priest River is hereby
prohibited and shall be unlawful except under emergency circumstances where the
use of air compression brakes is necessary to prevent an accident or injury to
persons or property. (Ord. 570, 3-2-2015)
6-4-2: VIOLATION:
Unless otherwise provided for under Idaho motor vehicle laws, a violation of
any provision of this chapter shall be assessed a civil assessment, payable to
the city clerk within fifteen (15) days of receipt of the complaint of such
violation, in the amount set forth in section
1-4-5 of this code. Upon a fourth violation the person or entity shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code for each violation.
(Ord. 570, 3-2-2015; amd. Ord. 631, 9-5-2023)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS AND SIDEWALKS
SECTION:
7-1-1: Standards Adopted
7-1-2: Encroachments
7-1-3: Snow And Ice Removal
7-1-4: Alley Maintenance And Snow Removal
7-1-1: STANDARDS ADOPTED:
   A.   There exist manuals, standards and specifications for uniform street
and sidewalk construction, repair, maintenance and traffic control published by
the local highway technical assistance council (LHTAC), Idaho transportation
department (ITD), the Idaho standards for public works construction executive
committee (ISPWC) and the federal highway administration (FHA). More
specifically, these manuals, standards and specifications are:
      1.   Manual for use of public right of way permits for utilities and
encroachments, as published and periodically revised by the LHTAC;
      2.   Manual for use of public right of way standard approach policy, as
published and periodically revised by the LHTAC;
      3.   Manual for streets and highways, as published and periodically
revised by the LHTAC;
      4.   "Idaho Standards For Public Works Construction", as published and
periodically revised by the ISPWC;
      5.   Idaho transportation department standards for highway construction,
as published and periodically revised by the ITD;
      6.   "Manual On Uniform Traffic Control Devices" (MUTCD), as published
and periodically revised by the FHA;
      7.   Idaho transportation department catalog of stormwater best
management practices (BMPs) for highway construction and maintenance, as
published and periodically revised by the ITD.
   B.   The most recent editions of these manuals, standards and specifications
are hereby adopted by reference as the street, sidewalk and public right of way
construction, repair and maintenance standards and specifications of the city.
   C.   A copy of all such manuals, standards and specifications shall be kept
on file by the city. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
7-1-2: ENCROACHMENTS:
   A.   Permit Requirements:
      1.   It is the responsibility of any person to first secure a right of
way encroachment permit from the city before beginning any construction,
maintenance or repair project within a city street, alley, sidewalk or right of
way.
      2.   Fees for encroachment permits shall be established by resolution of
the city council.
   B.   Utility Poles:
      1.   All utility poles hereafter set in the city shall be set within the
line established by the city. Upon proper notification by the city that any
street, alley or right of way is to be widened, vacated, paved or changed, any
person having poles set in said street, alley or right of way of the city shall
remove their poles therefrom and move them to the proper established line.
      2.   This subsection is intended to apply to all persons, companies or
corporations now having franchises granted to them by the city, or who may
hereafter obtain such franchise, or who may be operating or carrying on any
business within the city requiring use of such poles.
      3.   The right to amend, alter or repeal this section is hereby reserved.
   C.   Right Of Way Obstructions: No person shall obstruct any city sidewalk,
street, alley or right of way at any time for the sale or storage of any goods,
wares or merchandise or for any event or gathering of people without first
having obtained the permission of and having met the conditions set forth by
the city council.
Violations of any of the provisions of this section or failure to comply with
any of its requirements shall constitute a misdemeanor and upon conviction,
subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day such violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
7-1-3: SNOW AND ICE REMOVAL:
   A.   Removal Requirements:
      1.   It shall be the duty of the owner or occupant of any premises
abutting or adjoining any public sidewalk to remove all snow and/or ice from
such sidewalk whenever any such snow and/or ice reaches a depth of two inches
(2") or greater.
      2.   Unless otherwise provided, snow removed from any sidewalk or parking
area within the city shall not be thrown, shoveled or placed in the streets or
gutters of the city. In areas of the city where snow is regularly picked up by
the city and hauled from the streets, only snow removed from sidewalks within
the right of way shall be permitted to be placed in the streets and gutters.
(Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
      3.   Except as provided under subsection A2 of this section, snow shall
not be thrown, shoveled or placed onto a city right of way or alley.
Furthermore, snow removed from any property, residential or commercial, shall
not be thrown, shoveled or placed on the property of another owner without the
permission of said property owner, nor shall snow be thrown, shoveled or placed
so as to block the view of drivers at street intersections. (Ord. 493, 12-18-
2006)
   B.   Failure To Comply: Upon failure of an owner or occupant to comply with
the provisions of this section, the city shall have the right to remove such
snow and/or ice and assess the cost thereof against the premises abutting the
sidewalk. Such assessment is to be certified to the county assessor and such
charge shall be placed on the assessment roll and collected in the same manner
as other municipal taxes are collected.
Violations of any of the provisions of this section or failure to comply with
any of its requirements shall constitute a misdemeanor and upon conviction,
subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day such violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
7-1-4: ALLEY MAINTENANCE AND SNOW REMOVAL:
   A.   A property owner may petition the City Council for alley maintenance
and snow removal if the following conditions exist:
      1.   The alley serves as sole vehicular access to a parcel of property,
and
      2.   The sole access to the property was in existence prior to December
31, 2019.
   B.   If a Petition is granted under Subsection A, the City shall ensure the
following:
      1.   The Alley will be graded annually on an as-needed basis, and
      2.   Snow will be removed from Alley in the same manner and time frame as
third priority streets.
   C.   If a Petition is granted under Subsection A, it shall not relieve
Property Owners of obligations under
10-5-1(F).
   D.   No Building Permits shall be issued to a property owner without access
from an existing road or a new proposed roadway approved by the City of Priest
River. (Ord. 610, 2-3-2020)
CHAPTER 2
TREES AND SHRUBS
SECTION:
7-2-1: Owner's Responsibilities
7-2-2: Tree And Shrub Maintenance
7-2-3: Damage To Trees Or Shrubs
7-2-4: Prohibited Plantings And Species
7-2-5: Failure To Comply
7-2-6: Trees On City Property
7-2-1: OWNER'S RESPONSIBILITIES:
Any owner or occupant of any real property within the city shall have the
following responsibilities, and a violation of this section shall constitute a
misdemeanor:
   A.   Trim all trees overhanging any public sidewalk to a height of not less
than eight feet (8').
   B.   Trim all trees overhanging any public thoroughfare to a height of
fourteen feet (14').
   C.   Remove all hedges, shrubberies, fences, tree limbs or other obstruction
that may constitute a sight obstruction to the motoring public 1 . (Ord. 482,
6-5-2006)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsection 7-2-2A2 of this chapter.
7-2-2: TREE AND SHRUB MAINTENANCE:
   A.   Requirements:
      1.   Any owner or occupant of any real property shall maintain all hedges
and shrubbery adjacent to public sidewalks so that no part of such hedges and
shrubbery shall extend over any part of a public sidewalk.
      2.   Any owner or occupant of any real property within the city shall
remove from his property any structure, hedge, shrubbery, fence, wall, tree
limbs or other sight obstruction of any nature, except public traffic signs,
buildings and trees, where the sight obstructions constitute a potential
traffic hazard. The above sight obstructions shall not extend more than three
feet (3') nor less than ten feet (10') in height above the existing centerline
roadway elevation within the vision triangle of vehicle operators. The
boundaries of the vision triangle are defined by measuring from the
intersection of the edges of the two (2) adjacent roadways forty feet (40')
along each roadway and connecting the two (2) points with a straight line. The
bushes, shrubs, plants and structures in the area of a corner lot that extends
thirty feet (30') back in both directions from the point of the intersection
along the gutter line must not be more than thirty inches (30") tall and cannot
obstruct clear vision.
   B.   Violations: Violations of any of the provisions of this chapter or
failure to comply with any of its requirements shall constitute a misdemeanor
and upon conviction, subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day such violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
7-2-3: DAMAGE TO TREES OR SHRUBS:
It is unlawful for any person, not the owner thereof, or without lawful
authority to do so, wilfully to injure, deface, disfigure or destroy any tree
or shrub, or to injure, destroy, cut or pick any flower or plant located either
on private ground or on any public place or thoroughfare. A violation of this
section shall constitute a misdemeanor. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
7-2-4: PROHIBITED PLANTINGS AND SPECIES:
   A.   Prohibitions:
      1.   No person shall plant any tree, hedge or shrubbery within any city
right of way without first having received permission from the city council.
      2.   Under no circumstances shall a person plant any of the following
species of tree, hedge or shrubbery within a city right of way:
         Ailanthus
         American elm
         Box elder
         Cottonwood
         Fruit trees (except ornamental types)
         Mountain ash
         Nut trees
         Oregon or big leaf maple
         Poplar
         Willow
   B.   Violations: Violations of any of the provisions of this chapter or
failure to comply with any of its requirements shall constitute a misdemeanor
and upon conviction, subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. Each day such violation continues shall be considered a
separate offense. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
7-2-5: FAILURE TO COMPLY:
Upon failure of an owner or occupant to comply with the provisions of this
chapter, the city shall have the right to remove such tree branches, shrubbery
or hedge and assess the cost thereof against the premises abutting the sidewalk
or right of way. Such assessment shall be certified to the county assessor and
such charge shall be placed on the assessment roll and collected in the same
manner as other municipal taxes are collected. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
7-2-6: TREES ON CITY PROPERTY:
The governing body of the city is provided full and complete control over all
trees which are outside the property lines of privately owned real estate.
(Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
CHAPTER 3
STREET NAMING AND ADDRESSING SYSTEM
SECTION:
7-3-1: Authority, Jurisdiction And Purpose
7-3-2: Implementation, Administration And Approvals
7-3-3: Language And Definitions
7-3-4: Procedures And Standards
7-3-5: Enforcement And Administration
7-3-1: AUTHORITY, JURISDICTION AND PURPOSE:
   A.   Title: This chapter shall be known as the PRIEST RIVER STREET NAMING
AND ADDRESSING SYSTEM ORDINANCE.
   B.   Authority And Jurisdiction:
      1.   This chapter is authorized by article XII, section 2 of the Idaho
constitution and Idaho Code sections 31-714, 31-801, 40-604 and 67-6518.
      2.   In addition to the general authorities set out above, this chapter
is authorized by Idaho Code title 50, chapter 13 and title 67, chapter 65. The
regulations contained in this chapter shall apply to the naming of all streets
and the addressing of all structures and parcels within the incorporated
territory of the city of Priest River, or as mutually defined by both city and
county under the requirements of Idaho Code 50-1306 or 67-6526.
   C.   Purpose And Applicability: This chapter further implements portions of
the Priest River comprehensive plan and supplements the zoning and subdivision
regulations. Its purpose is to provide city residents with a uniform and
standardized system of street naming and addressing to:
      1.   Minimize future street name and addressing conflicts.
      2.   Provide a database for city records and enhanced 911 service.
      3.   Expedite property identification by emergency services.
      4.   Comply with the following addressing guidelines: National Emergency
Number Association (NENA) addressing and mapping standards, Verizon E-
9-1-1 addressing guidelines "practice 444-400-015", and U.S. postal service
publication 28, "Postal Addressing Standards". (Ord. 523, 6-1-2009)
7-3-2: IMPLEMENTATION, ADMINISTRATION AND APPROVALS:
   A.   Implementation And Responsibilities:
      1.   The administrator and his/her designees shall have the
responsibility of implementing, enforcing, and maintaining an addressing and
street naming standard as defined by this chapter.
      2.   In the event that violations of this chapter are not corrected by
the date required herein, Priest River may perform the work and pursue remedies
as provided in this section.
      3.   Property owners are responsible for placing and maintaining numeric
identification and for erecting private street signs in accordance with this
chapter. Posting of addresses and street names should be done within four (4)
months of issuance of the address or street name. Private street signs shall be
erected under the guidelines of the current Priest River street standards
manual.
      4.   The Priest River public works department is responsible for erecting
and maintaining public street signs at street intersections.
      5.   The property owner is responsible for the designation of the access
points on the public or private street and installation and maintenance of all
required street signs. The access point(s) designated by the owner shall be
utilized to determine the address of the parcel. Such access points are subject
to review and approval of the city to ensure that they are accessible to
emergency service providers.
      6.   All addresses shall comply with the addressing guidelines outlined
in subsection
7-3-1C of this chapter. The order of precedence will be NENA, Verizon E-
9-1-1 addressing guidelines, and the United States post office addressing
standards.
      7.   For the purposes of addressing and street naming, the city clerk's
office will house and maintain all official data.
   B.   Administrator: The city public works supervisor shall be empowered to
exercise the powers delegated to him/her by this title of administrator. The
administrator may appoint specific designees to assist with carrying out the
duties set forth by this chapter.
   C.   Approvals Required:
      1.   Before any street is named, approval shall be obtained from the
administrator.
      2.   Official street names shall be maintained on the Priest River street
name list.
      3.   Before any addresses are posted, approval shall be obtained from the
administrator.
      4.   If, in any instance, the administrator fails to act or carry out
his/her responsibilities according to the regulations contained herein, the
council may assume the duties of the administrator, as herein specified. (Ord.
523, 6-1-2009)
7-3-3: LANGUAGE AND DEFINITIONS:
   A.   Construction Of Language: The rules and definitions contained in this
section shall be observed and applied, except when the context clearly
indicates:
      1.   The word "shall" is mandatory and not discretionary.
      2.   The words "should" and "may" indicate the use of discretion.
      3.   When consistent with this text, words used in the present tense
include the future; words used in the future tense include the present.
   B.   Definitions:
   ACCESS: The primary means of vehicular ingress/egress to a parcel or
structure.
   ADDRESS OR SERVICE ADDRESS: The official city assigned unique identification
number for a parcel and/or structure that uniquely defines its location within
the city. This address may be used for mail delivery if allowed by the U.S.
postal service.
   ADMINISTRATOR: Priest River staff appointed by the city council whose duties
are to exercise the powers delegated to him/her by this chapter.
   APPROACH: Any vehicular entrance upon a city right of way, other than a
"driveway".
   CITY COUNCIL: Elected officials who are vested with all executive and
legislative authority of the city and whose powers, authority and duties are
outlined in Idaho Code title 50.
   COMMON DRIVEWAY: A vehicular access serving three (3) or four (4) parcels,
which has an approach to a public street or connects to a private street.
Common driveways shall be named.
   CUL-DE-SAC: A dead end street that provides a turnaround at its terminus.
   DEVELOPER: An individual, firm, corporation, partnership, association,
syndicate, trust or other legal entity that executes applications and initiates
proceedings for subdivision of land. The developer need not be the owner of the
land, but he shall be the agent of the owner.
   DRIVEWAY: For the purposes of this chapter, the term "driveway" shall mean a
vehicular entrance upon a public or private streetway, or connects to a common
driveway, which provides access to a fourplex or smaller multi-family dwelling,
or two (2) or fewer single-family residential lots or parcels. Driveways shall
not be named.
   DWELLING: A habitable structure.
   LOT: A designated parcel, tract or area of land established by plat or as
otherwise permitted by law, to be used, developed or built upon as a unit.
   MUTCD: The latest edition of the "Manual On Uniform Traffic Control Devices"
as published by the federal highway administration.
   OWNER: The legal property owner as shown by the latest information provided
by the Bonner County assessor's office.
   PLAT: A map of representation of a named subdivision of land into lots,
blocks, and streets to be recorded as a public document.
   PRIMARY ACCESS POINT: That primary point designated on a private or public
street, or common driveway from which the driveway to a parcel or structure
intersects the private or public street or common driveway.
   PRIVATE STREET: Means of vehicular access which has not been accepted for
maintenance by the board or a public highway agency and which does not meet the
definition of a "driveway", "common driveway" or "public street".
   PUBLIC HIGHWAY AGENCY: The public street agency having jurisdiction for
primary and secondary streets in the incorporated areas of the city.
   PUBLIC STREET: A street, thoroughfare, alley, or highway; a right of way for
public use that provides vehicular access, as defined by Idaho Code sections
40-117 and 50-1301.
   SERVIENT PROPERTY: Property over which a private street passes, or property
served by a private street easement. (Ord. 523, 6-1-2009)
7-3-4: PROCEDURES AND STANDARDS:
   A.   Street Designations: Designation of new streets within the incorporated
areas of Priest River shall be in accordance with the following guidelines:
      1.   All named streets that extend from incorporated areas into
unincorporated areas shall retain the same name.
      2.   Streets which have a generally north-south directional course should
be designated as a street. Streets which have a generally east-west directional
course should be designated an avenue.
      3.   Streets which do not have a definite directional course shall be
assigned a designation at the discretion of the administrator.
      4.   A dead end street or cul-de-sac less than one thousand feet (1,000')
in length, when not an extension of an existing street or a continuation of a
proposed street, should be called a court.
      5.   A street that has its ingress and egress on the same street shall be
designated a circle or loop.
      6.   A street that circles back upon itself shall be designated as a
circle.
      7.   Special scenic routes or park drives may be designated parkway upon
review and approval by the administrator.
      8.   When a proposed street is in general alignment with an existing
street, and the proposed street is planned to be a continuation of the existing
street, the existing name and designation should be maintained given no
conflict with subsection B of this section.
      9.   Duplicate street names are prohibited. Existing duplicated names
should be corrected in accordance with this chapter.
   B.   Addressing Procedures:
      1.   General Procedures: All address numbers shall conform to the
addressing system outlined by this chapter. The general standards to be used in
developing an address are as follows:
         a.   The address system shall be based on a mileage system by
measuring to the one one-thousandth (1/1,000) of a mile. The point of beginning
for generally north/south streets shall be U.S. 2 and the point of beginning
for generally east/west streets shall be SR 57. All streets that continue
across U.S. 2 shall be prefixed north or south and all streets that continue
across SR 57 shall be prefixed east or west.
         b.   Addressing for state highways shall be based on mile markers.
(Example: If a driveway is on Highway 2 and it is between mile marker 5 and 6
and the measurement from mile marker 5 to the driveway is 0.425 miles, the
address for this driveway is 5425 Highway 2.)
         c.   A standard of one thousand (1,000) addressing units per mile is
hereby established.
         d.   Even numbers shall be used on west and south sides of the street,
and odd numbers should be used on the east and north sides.
      2.   Streets:
         a.   If a building has a number of entrances, each serving separate
occupants, then the building shall be assigned an address and the individual
units assigned unit numbers. (Example: 24 Birch Rd., Suite 3.)
         b.   An addressing scheme for multi-family dwelling structures shall
be approved by the administrator that is in accord with the standards and
guidelines outlined in subsection
7-3-1C4 of this chapter. In general, a multi-family dwelling structure with one
main entrance should be assigned one number with the owner of the structure
responsible for providing designated individual numbering of each unit before
an address will be issued to the structure. (Example: 15864 Maas Loop, Apt.
101.) In some cases where there are several multi-family dwelling structures
sharing one main access, it may be necessary to name the streets within the
complex and provide individual street numbers to the buildings. This
determination will be made by the administrator on a case by case basis.
         c.   An addressing scheme for mobile home parks structures shall be
approved by the administrator that is in accord with E-
9-1-1 addressing standards. In general, mobile home parks should have names for
the streets within the complex and individual street numbers should be assigned
by the city for each mobile home space. Alphanumeric combinations shall not be
used for numbering individual spaces.
         d.   If a street or driveway accesses three (3) or more properties, it
shall be assigned a street name and the parcels shall be addressed in
accordance with this chapter.
         e.   Parcels with structure(s), or bare land parcels, which are
accessed by a driveway, shall be assigned an address at the point where the
driveway intersects a named street.
         f.   The street name and address for any dwelling should be determined
by the street on which the dwelling fronts. However, in those instances where
access is from a different street and the dwelling is not visible from the
fronting street, or if the dwelling is not readily accessible to emergency
personnel from the fronting street, the street name and address will be
assigned based on the access street.
         g.   For parcels that are accessed by multiple driveways, the owner
shall designate a primary access point that will be used for address
assignment. Such access points are subject to review and approval of the city
to ensure that they are accessible to emergency service providers. If the
property owner does not designate a primary access point, the city shall make
the official determination to allow the proper addressing of the property.
         h.   Circular and loop streets should begin numbering at the lower
numbered intersection, with odd and even numbers following the set standard.
         i.   For circle streets, the numbering should begin at its origin and
proceed in a counterclockwise direction around the circle using a consecutive
numerical order and odd/even numbers consistent with the beginning of the
street as if the street were straight.
         j.   Parcels served by a common driveway that access two (2) parcels
should be assigned an address at the point where the access intersects a public
or private street or named common driveway. Each property shall be assigned a
different address. If the city issues multiple addresses to a parcel pursuant
to this section, the city may also require that the common driveway be named in
the same manner as private streets.
         k.   Fractional addresses (56981/2 Happy Trail Street) and hyphenated
address numbers (632-58 Kennedy) shall not be used.
         l.   Parcels with multiple structures will be addressed on a case by
case basis.
      3.   Waterfront:
         a.   A shoreline distance based system may be used by the emergency
service agencies to assign numerical points to facilitate emergency responses.
These marine response identification numbers shall not be used as addresses
except for those parcels that do not have any access other than by water.
         b.   Marine response identification numbers should be based on a
shoreline distance measurement. Starting points shall be established at a
readily identified point on the water body and numbered consecutively. Odd and
even numbers may occur along the same shore.
   C.   Street Naming Standards:
      1.   It is hereby established that the following rules and regulations
for the naming of streets shall apply. All official street names shall be
assembled in the Bonner County road name list. Additions and amendments to the
list shall be made by the administrator. All new street names or changes to
names shall be established in accordance with the standards and procedures
hereinafter set forth. If possible, surnames should not be used.
      2.   The following standards shall be used in determining and approving
street names:
         a.   All proposed street names shall be submitted to the administrator
for review and approval.
         b.   Street names should be easy to communicate (e.g., across
electronic communication devices) and shall not be offensive to the standards
of good taste.
         c.   There shall be no duplication of names by sound or spelling
(example: Briar Street, Brier Street).
         d.   Variations of the same name with a different street designation
shall be prohibited within the first word of the two (2) word title or in the
street extension (example: Pine Street, Pine Drive, White Pine Street, White
Lilly Lane).
         e.   When a proposed street is in general alignment with an existing
street, and the proposed street is or planned to be a continuation of the
existing street, the existing name and designation should be maintained.
         f.   Where a proposed street connects, or aligns with, two (2)
different streets each having different names, the administrator shall decide
the name to be used, giving consideration to the length, classification, period
of usage and number of residents affected.
