         g.   Both "L" shaped and "T" shaped streets should carry the same name
if either leg is one hundred feet (100') or less in length. "L" shaped and "T"
shaped streets over one hundred feet (100') in length each should carry a
different name on each leg of the "L" or the "T". This determination shall be
made on a case by case basis.
         h.   In general, street names should consist of no more than three (3)
words or contain over sixteen (16) letters in length including spaces, unless
otherwise approved by the administrator. The street direction (N, S, E, W) and
designation (e.g., street, lane, court, etc.) is not included. All names should
conform to this limitation except where existing names are to be continued due
to alignments.
         i.   There shall be no duplication of existing names. The city will
recognize Bonner County as the repository for the official list of street names
for the city.
         j.   No street shall have more than one name.
         k.   No street name shall contain the words north, south, east, or
west, or any combination thereof, within the street name except for use as a
prefix to names of streets crossing either U.S. 2 or SR 57.
   D.   New Streets Or Existing Unnamed Streets:
      1.   Any new street to be established within the city, public or private,
or any existing unnamed street, public or private, shall require a street name
approved by the administrator.
      2.   In the case of plats, approved street names shall be specified on
the final plat map.
   E.   Official Designation Of Existing Street Names: With the adoption of
this chapter, all streets named as a result of the city mapping and rural
addressing project for enhanced 911 shall be designated as the official street
names.
   F.   Renaming Streets:
      1.   Renaming Of Existing Duplicated Street Names: Where duplicate names
exist, streets should be renamed by the administrator to eliminate the
duplication. The administrator shall decide which streets shall be renamed
using the following criteria:
         a.   When the street was originally named.
         b.   The number of improved properties served by the street.
         c.   Other factors as deemed appropriate by the administrator.
         d.   When a street name within the incorporated area of the city is
duplicated by a street name within the county, the county shall work with the
city to decide which street shall be renamed.
      2.   Renaming Other Streets: In cases where property owners request to
change the name of a street which has an existing city approved name, the
property owners may petition the city. Property owner initiated requests under
this section shall require seventy five percent (75%) approval of property
owners abutting the street and the payment of an applicable fee and any other
costs incurred. Street names shall not be changed more frequently than once
every five (5) years.
   G.   Signage:
      1.   Physical Addresses: Physical address numbers shall be clearly
readable from the streetway, and shall contrast with background. If a structure
is more than seventy five feet (75') from the street, or is otherwise not
clearly visible from the street, its address shall be posted at the
intersection of its access street and public or private street. The address
sign should be no less than four feet (4') nor more than six feet (6') above
the ground and mounted on support structure not exceeding the standards listed
in section 8 of the "Street Standards Manual" (title 2, BCRC) published by the
Bonner County public works department. The view of the address from the street
must be unobstructed and maintained. All primary letters, numbers and symbols
should be a minimum of three and one-half inches (31/2") in height, with a one-
half inch (1/2") stroke, and should contrast with the background color. The
city shall not be liable for any damage to the address sign and support
structure. The city shall not be liable for any damage caused by the
installation of the address sign and support structure.
      2.   Marine Response Identification Numbers:
         a.   Where a marine response identification number is used as an
address for a parcel, the number should be posted on a pier, dock or other
waterfront appurtenance, no less than four feet (4') nor more than six feet
(6') above the ground or high water line. The sign must be clearly readable to
emergency providers arriving by boat.
         b.   In cases where the marine response identification number is not
used as an address (where street access is available and a street address has
been issued), the marine response identification number should be posted in
accordance with the policies of the emergency service providers.
   H.   Street Sign Standards:
      1.   General: Street signs shall be placed in accordance with subsection
H2 of this section to be clearly visible at intersections. All primary letters,
numbers, and symbols shall be a minimum of four inches (4") in height, with a
one-half inch (1/2") stroke, and shall be reflectorized and contrasting with
the background color of the sign in accordance with the "Manual On Uniform
Traffic Control Devices" (MUTCD). Specifically, public street signs shall be
green with white lettering. Private street signs shall be blue with white
letters. All public and private street signs shall be constructed and installed
to the standards of the city. Signs shall be installed within one hundred
twenty (120) days of notice of approval of the street name or before any
construction starts on any structure accessed by that street, whichever is
later.
      2.   Installation Standards: Proper positioning of signs is essential to
obtain maximum safety, efficiency and observance. Signs should be installed in
accord with the corresponding public and private streets standards manual
adopted by the city along with standards listed within the "Manual On Uniform
Traffic Control Devices" (MUTCD). (Ord. 523, 6-1-2009)
7-3-5: ENFORCEMENT AND ADMINISTRATION:
   A.   Enforcement:
      1.   Violations: It shall be unlawful for any person to:
         a.   Erect or install a street name sign not in accordance with this
chapter.
         b.   Remove, alter, change, or deface a street name sign or address
identification erected or installed as provided herein.
         c.   Place or post addresses not approved by this chapter.
      2.   Penalty: Any person who violates or fails to comply with any of the
provisions of this chapter shall be subject to penalty and enforcement as
follows:
The owner, or other person, who may be responsible for compliance with the
provisions of this chapter, who has been notified of the violation or failure
to comply, fails to comply and cure the violation within the time provided in
the notice, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. However, the city's
prosecuting attorney may elect to refrain from initiating criminal prosecution
on the violation or failure to comply if the violator brings the property into
compliance and pays to the city clerk within fifteen (15) days of receipt of
the complaint of such violation a civil assessment in the amount set forth in
section
1-4-5 of this code.
If there is not compliance and payment of the applicable penalties as set forth
above, the offense shall be punishable as provided in the general penalty
provisions set forth in section
1-4-1 of this code.
   B.   Administrative Procedures: The city council may, by resolution, adopt
administrative procedures, create fee schedules, etc., to facilitate
implementation of the purpose and intent of this chapter.
      1.   Amendments: The city council may amend, supplement or repeal the
regulations and provisions of this chapter in the manner prescribed by Idaho
Code. A proposed amendment, supplement or repeal may be originated by the city
council, administrator or by petition. All proposals not originating with the
administrator shall be referred to him/her for a report thereon before any
action is taken on the proposal by the city council.
      2.   Controversial Or Disputed Street Names: The administrator shall have
the discretion to refer any disputed street name, addressing issues or
controversial street name changes to the city council for approval or
resolution.
      3.   Appeals: Appeals concerning interpretation or administration of this
chapter may be filed by any affected person. Such appeals shall be filed within
a reasonable time of the action being appealed, not to exceed thirty (30) days,
by filing with the administrator a notice of appeal specifying the grounds of
the appeal. The administrator shall schedule a meeting with the council to hear
the appeal and shall provide written notice to the affected persons of the time
and place of the meeting. The affected persons and the administrator shall be
provided an opportunity to present the relevant issues to the board at that
meeting. The council's decision shall be final, and further recourse for the
affected persons shall be to the courts as provided by law.
      4.   Appeal Not Granted For Special Privilege Or Exception: An
administrative appeal shall not be granted if it would function as a grant of
special privilege or to provide an exception to the regulations contained
within this code.
(Ord. 523, 6-1-2009; amd. Ord. 549, 7-16-2012; Ord. 631, 9-5-2023)
CHAPTER 4
PUBLIC PARKS
SECTION:
7-4-1: General
7-4-2: Permit Process
7-4-3: Violation And Penalty
7-4-1: GENERAL:
   A.   Hours: The use of all public parks and recreation areas within the city
limits is prohibited without a permit from sunset to sunrise.
   B.   Park Closure: The mayor, or a duly authorized representative, may close
a park area or recreation facility at any time there is an apparent danger to
the persons using the property itself, or for any cause which would provide for
the safety and protection of the public. Remaining in an area closed by the
mayor or authorized representative is prohibited.
   C.   Exceptions: The provisions of this chapter do not apply to the
operation of city owned or operated vehicles or personnel while engaged in
official city business.
   D.   Overnight Camping: Overnight camping is prohibited except when
necessary for overnight security at multiday events.
   E.   Open Fires: Open fires are prohibited without a permit. No permit shall
be issued without a fire permit from the fire department.
   F.   Amplified Sound: Amplified sound, whether for speech, music, or
otherwise, is prohibited without first obtaining a city permit.
   G.   Model Airplanes, Boats, Cars Or Model Rockets: The operation of motor
driven airplanes, boats, cars or model rockets is prohibited on park property
without first obtaining a city permit.
   H.   Dumping: Dumping rocks, soil, grass clippings, branches, leaves,
equipment, vehicles, furniture, or any other item or material is prohibited.
   I.   Litter, Rubbish And Glass Containers: Carrying onto any park property
any garbage, trash or refuse is prohibited. Trash generated in the park must be
deposited in provided trash receptacles or carried off the park property. Glass
containers are prohibited.
   J.   Flora And Turf: Removing or injuring any form of plant life on park
property, including the removal of wood, turf, grass, soil, rock, sand and
gravel is prohibited except by a duly authorized city employee or authorized
contractor in the performance of their duties.
   K.   Animals: With the exception of service animals, dogs and cats are
prohibited on park property unless kept on a leash at all times and under full
control of the owner. The removal of feces of animals that defecate on park
property is required of the owner or custodian of said animal and such owner or
custodian shall have the means to do so in their possession. All pets may be
prohibited from parks for the duration of a permitted event. Livestock are not
allowed on park property without a permit. No animal shall be killed, harmed,
or removed from any park without government authority.
   L.   Motor Vehicles And Parking: Motor vehicles shall not be operated or
parked except on designated roadway or within designated markings without a
city permit.
   M.   Roller Skates And Skateboards: Except for the skatepark, roller skates,
skateboards and other similar items are prohibited from the parks unless a
permitted event specifically permits the use of such items. Motor vehicles are
prohibited in all parks except as necessary to set up a permitted event.
   N.   Alcoholic Beverages: Alcoholic beverages are prohibited within parks
except as may be authorized during an event after obtaining a city permit.
   O.   Fireworks: The possession or firing of firecrackers, rockets, torpedoes
or other fireworks on park property is prohibited. (See title 4, chapter 3 of
this code.) This subsection shall not apply to professional displays by
companies licensed by the state of Idaho in conjunction with a city permitted
event. (Ord. 547, 5-21-2012)
   P.   Firearms And Weapons: Discharging any firearm, air gun, slingshot, or
bow and arrow is prohibited on park property without a city permit. (Ord. 571,
3-2-2015)
   Q.   Interference: No person shall use, attempt to use, or interfere with
the use of any facility which is reserved for another person or group holding a
permit issued by the city.
   R.   Damage To Park Property: Persons causing damage or committing
vandalism, or parents of such persons under the age of eighteen (18), will be
held financially responsible for the full amount of damages. (Ord. 547, 5-21-
2012)
7-4-2: PERMIT PROCESS:
   A.   Use Of Parks: The city's park areas may be made available for the use
of persons and groups subject to the issuance of a permit and the payment of
fees. Use of any park for preadvertised assemblies may not be made without the
issuance of a permit. All applications for use of city parks shall be signed by
an adult twenty one (21) years of age or over who shall be responsible for
compliance with the terms of the permit.
   B.   Application For Use:
      1.   The mayor shall reserve the right to grant or deny all applications
for the use of parks within the city. This authority is hereby delegated to the
city clerk and/or chief of police.
      2.   Requests for use shall be made a minimum of fourteen (14) days and a
maximum of six (6) months prior to the date of requested use. Exception:
Applications that will include a separate alcoholic beverage catering permit
for use in a park must be made in person a minimum of thirty (30) days prior to
the event.
      3.   The application for a permit shall include, but not be limited to,
the following information:
         a.   Name of the applicant, the sponsoring organization(s), and name
of the person in charge of the proposed activity;
         b.   Address and telephone number of applicant(s);
         c.   Park being applied for and the area involved;
         d.   Starting time of the proposed activity;
         e.   Finish time of the proposed activity;
         f.   Number of persons expected;
         g.   Additional city personnel or items requested, such as barricades;
         h.   Nature of the proposed activity or activities, including
equipment and vehicles to be brought into the park, duration and nature of the
use of any amplified sound whether speech, music, or otherwise;
         i.   Fees charged and monies collected;
         j.   Individual(s) who will receive monies collected and purpose for
money;
         k.   Notice of requirement of certificate of co-insurance for public
liability, in the form of attachment to application, if required.
   C.   Liability: All persons to whom a use permit is granted must agree in
writing to hold the city harmless and indemnify the city from any and all
liability for injury to persons or property occurring as the result of the
activity sponsored by permittee, and said persons shall be liable to the city
for any and all damages to parks, equipment and buildings owned or controlled
by the city which result from the activity or permittee or is caused by any
participant in said activity. A person exercising any of the privileges
authorized by this policy does so at his own risk without liability on the part
of the city for any injury to persons or property resulting therefrom.
When an association or organization which carries public liability insurance
requests the use of city facilities, or when the city is involved with
scheduling and/or coordinating their activities, a certificate of co-insurance
naming the city as an additional insured must be filed with the city five (5)
days prior to the first day of use of facilities involved. The city may require
proof of liability insurance with limit of bodily injury and property damage of
not less than one million dollars ($1,000,000.00) and a certificate of co-
insurance for any group when it is determined that the planned activity is
judged to be other than a low risk activity.
   D.   Cleanup: The permittee is responsible to ensure all trash is picked up
and placed in the appropriate trash containers and that the park is left neat
and orderly. Any work performed by city crew to clean up after the permitted
use will be billed to the permittee.
   E.   Revocation Of Permit: Permit may be revoked if any terms or conditions
of the permit are violated by the permittee or any agent or employee of the
permittee.
   F.   Appeal Process: An applicant may appeal the decision of a city
representative regarding park use permits to the city council by contacting the
city clerk. (Ord. 547, 5-21-2012)
7-4-3: VIOLATION AND PENALTY:
A violation of any provision of this chapter shall be a misdemeanor and shall
be punished as provided in the general penalty in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 547, 5-21-2012)
TITLE 8
PUBLIC UTILITIES
CHAPTER 1
PUBLIC UTILITY SERVICES
SECTION:
8-1-1: Definitions
8-1-2: Utility Services User Application
8-1-3: Utility Service Charges Payment Policy
8-1-4: Delinquent Utility Service Charges Collection Policy
8-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
BACKFLOW: Any flow, actual or potential, intentional or otherwise, of any
liquid, gas or substance from a customer service back into the city water
system.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION: The elimination of any backflow through the use of a
backflow prevention assembly.
BACKFLOW PREVENTION ASSEMBLY: Any device approved by the purveyor that will
eliminate backflow into the city water system.
BASE UNIT: A single-family residence, apartment or commercial unit.
BASE UNIT CHARGE: The monthly amount charged for sewer service for each base
unit, and shall be as prescribed by the city council and specified in the rate
schedule.
CITY: The municipal corporation known as the city of Priest River, or the city
council of the city of Priest River, or the staff of the city of Priest River.
The exact meaning shall depend upon the context used.
CITY LIMITS: The limits of the incorporated city of Priest River.
CITY SEWER SYSTEM: The sewer system, governed and administered by the city, the
purpose of which is the collection, transportation, treatment and disposal of
sanitary sewage. The city sewer system includes all collection, transportation,
treatment and disposal facilities.
CITY WATER SYSTEM: The water system of the city of Priest River, governed and
administered by the city, intended or used for fire protection, human
consumption or other domestic or nondomestic purposes for the citizens of the
city and areas under the jurisdiction of the city. The city water system
includes all source, treatment, storage, transmission and distribution
facilities.
CONTAMINATION: The introduction into, or the presence of, in the city water
system any liquid, gas or substance that, when present in the city water system
above an acceptable level (as determined by the DEQ), may adversely affect the
health of the water consumer and/or the aesthetic qualities of the water.
CROSS CONNECTION: Any physical arrangement connecting the city water system,
directly or indirectly, with anything capable of causing contamination of the
city water system as a result of a backflow.
CUSTOMER: An owner who has been granted utility services, or any portion
thereof, by completing an application for utility services.
CUSTOMER SERVICE: A physical connection furnishing water between the city water
system and a customer's water system.
DELINQUENT NOTICE: A notice sent by the city to a delinquent customer informing
them that they are delinquent on payment of utility service charges. Such
notice shall be contained in the regular billing of utility service charges
mailed to the customer. The delinquent notice shall contain information as to
the amount of utility service charges due and payable, and a notice that in
fifteen (15) days, a twenty four (24) hour notice shall be issued. Such
delinquent notice shall be mailed to the customer's last known address by
regular mail, and its receipt shall be presumed.
DEQ: The Idaho department of health and welfare, department of environmental
quality.
MULTI-UNIT: A single parcel with more than one residential or commercial
occupancy unit.
OWNER: The legal owner of record, or the legal representative of the legal
owner of record, of a particular real property.
PUBLIC UTILITY SYSTEM: Any water system or sewer system, or part thereof,
constructed within city rights of way, or upon city property, or property under
the jurisdiction of the city, intended to be connected to a city water system
or city sewer system, the purpose of which is to procure, treat, transport,
store, deliver or measure water for the city water system, or to collect,
transport, treat, measure or dispose of wastewater, or wastewater treatment
byproducts, for the city sewer system.
RATE SCHEDULE: The current resolution, passed by the city council, specifying
the schedule of water and sewer connection fees, and other charges and fees,
charged by the city.
SEWER SYSTEM: The network of piping, manholes, cleanouts, pumping stations and
other facilities and appurtenances used to construct, in city rights of way and
easements, a system, the purpose of which is to provide for the collection and
transportation of sanitary sewage to a wastewater treatment facility. A sewer
system shall, at least at one point, be connected to the existing city sewer
system.
TWENTY FOUR HOUR NOTICE: A notice hand delivered to a delinquent customer
notifying the delinquent customer of the city's intention to discontinue water
service, as a means of enforcement of payment of utility service charges, in
twenty four (24) hours. Such notice shall be delivered no less than twenty four
(24) hours before the city effects discontinuation. Such notice shall be posted
at the delinquent customer's service address, and shall contain the date and
time of water service discontinuation, the current and past due utility service
charges, and the terms and cost of water service recontinuation.
UTILITY SERVICE CHARGES: Any and all charges billed by the city for utility
services and shall include all fees, fines, remediation charges, utility
services discontinuation and recontinuation charges and other penalties or
charges legally assessed by the city or by a county, state or federal court in
accordance with the provisions of this code.
UTILITY SERVICES: All water, sewer, refuse collection and related services, or
any portion thereof, provided by, or under the authority of, the city.
WATER SYSTEM: The network of piping, water service lines and meters, valves,
fire hydrants, fittings, pumps, storage facilities and appurtenances used to
construct, in city rights of way and easements, a system, the purpose of which
is to provide for the delivery of potable and fire protection water. A water
system shall, at least at one point, be connected to the existing city water
system. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-1-2: UTILITY SERVICES USER APPLICATION:
   A.   All applications for utility services shall be made by and in the name
of the owner, and shall be made by completing an application for utility
services provided by the city.
   B.   Owners of properties presently being supplied with utility services
under a name other than that of the owner shall complete and submit an
application for utility services in the name of the owner, in accordance with
subsection A of this section, within thirty (30) days of official notification
to do so by the city. Failure of an owner to comply with this section shall
result in discontinuation of utility services.
   C.   The owner of any property being supplied utility services by the city
shall be held legally responsible for payment for all current and past due
utility service charges, and for any and all costs incurred by the city for
collection of these utility service charges.
   D.   All requests for discontinuation of utility services shall be made by
the owner, and shall be made by completing a request for discontinuation of
utility services.
   E.   No applications for utility services shall be approved by the city for
any property that has an unpaid utility service charges balance. (Ord. 482, 6-
5-2006)
8-1-3: UTILITY SERVICE CHARGES PAYMENT POLICY:
   A.   It is the policy of the city that all utility service charges are due
and payable within fifteen (15) days of billing. Any utility service charges
not paid in full by the date due shall be considered delinquent, and shall be
subject to collection in accordance with the provisions of this code. (Ord.
532, 5-3-2010)
   B.   Any utility service charges, or portion thereof, that is disputed by
the customer must be done so in writing to the city clerk. If the city clerk
cannot resolve the dispute, it shall be presented to the city council for
resolution at the next regularly scheduled city council meeting. The decision
of the city council shall be final. Any utility service charges, or portion
thereof, that is not in dispute by the customer shall be paid in full by the
date due, or shall be considered delinquent and shall be subject to collection
in accordance with the provisions of this code. For the purposes of this code,
the monthly minimum water service charge, water meter demand charge, and sewer
base unit charge shall be considered not to be in dispute. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006;
amd. Ord. 532, 5-3-2010)
8-1-4: DELINQUENT UTILITY SERVICE CHARGES COLLECTION POLICY:
   A.   Lien Conditions:
      1.   Recovery By City:
         a.   The city shall have a lien upon any premises served with utility
services to the extent of such delinquent utility service charges incurred
after the effective date hereof, and such delinquent utility service charges
shall be subject to recovery in the manners set forth in this chapter.
         b.   The liens referred to in this chapter are preferred to any lien,
mortgage or other encumbrance which may have attached subsequent to the time
utility services were furnished; also, to any lien, mortgage or other
encumbrance of which the city had no notice, and which was unrecorded at the
time utility services were furnished.
      2.   Lien Foreclosure Authority: It shall be the duty of the city
attorney, at the direction of the city council, to foreclose upon such liens as
described in this chapter, and to bring appropriate actions as necessary for
the collection thereof.
   B.   Enforcement Of Payment Policy:
      1.   It is declared the policy of the city that enforcement of payment of
delinquent utility service charges shall be by discontinuation of water
service, or by foreclosure of a lien as specified in subsection A of this
section. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
      2.   Any utility service charges not paid within the time frame as
established in subsection
8-1-3A of this chapter shall be declared delinquent, whereupon the city clerk
shall provide the delinquent customer with a delinquent notice. (Ord. 482, 6-5-
2006; amd. Ord. 532, 5-3-2010)
      3.   A delinquent customer shall have fifteen (15) days from the time of
issuance of a delinquent notice in which to file a request for a hearing before
the city council in order to show cause why their water service should not be
discontinued. Such requests for hearings shall be made in writing by the
customer and addressed to the city clerk. The city clerk shall schedule a
hearing at a time and date convenient for the city council, and shall notify
the customer of such. The city council shall receive all relevant evidence and
shall issue its decision based upon that evidence. The decision of the city
council shall be final. Until such time as the city council reaches their
decision, discontinuance of water service of the delinquent customer shall be
delayed. Delinquent customers failing to show adequate cause before the city
council shall have the next business day to pay all utility service charges
billed. Failure to pay all utility service charges billed by the end of the
next business day shall result in discontinuation of water service at eight
o'clock (8:00) A.M. of the following business day.
   C.   Twenty Four Hour Notice:
      1.   The city clerk shall cause delinquent customers to be issued a
twenty four (24) hour notice no sooner than fifteen (15) days after issuance of
a delinquent notice.
      2.   There shall be imposed upon a delinquent customer a penalty charge
if issued a twenty four (24) hour notice. Such penalty charge shall be as
specified by resolution and such charge shall be added to the customer's
utility service charges balance due.
   D.   Discontinuation Of Utility Services Authorized:
      1.   The city is authorized to discontinue water service of delinquent
customers served with a twenty four (24) hour notice twenty four (24) hours
after issuance of such notice. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
      2.   No delinquent customer shall, after having water service
discontinued in accordance with this chapter, thereafter be provided with water
service until such time as all delinquent and current utility service charges
have been paid in full. Delinquent customers whose water service has been
discontinued shall also pay a recontinuation fee. Such fee shall be as
specified by resolution, and shall be added to the customer's utility service
charges. (Ord. 532, 5-3-2010)
      3.   Delinquent customers whose water service has been discontinued shall
also pay any additional fees, if adverse conditions exist that affect the
accessibility of the curb valve or the meter valve. Such additional fees shall
be added to the customer's utility service charges. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
CHAPTER 2
UTILITY SERVICES RATES AND CHARGES
SECTION:
8-2-1: Water Meters Required
8-2-2: Utility Service Charges
8-2-3: Fire Hydrant And Tank Truck Filling Charges
8-2-4: Water Service Turnon/Turnoff
8-2-5: Review Of Rate Schedule
8-2-6: Utility Improvement Bond Assessments
8-2-1: WATER METERS REQUIRED:
Except for charges imposed for unmetered tank truck filling in this chapter, it
is the declared policy of the city that all service charges for water shall be
computed by a water meter, and that all water meters used for computation of
water service charges shall be supplied, owned and maintained by the city. The
penalty for failure of a customer to comply with any part of this section shall
be the immediate discontinuation of the customer's water service. (Ord. 482, 6-
5-2006)
8-2-2: UTILITY SERVICE CHARGES:
   A.   Water Service:
      1.   There are imposed monthly water service charges upon each
residential and commercial customer receiving water service from the city. Such
water service charges shall include a monthly minimum charge, overage
consumption charge, and, for services with meters larger than one inch (1"), a
demand charge, and shall be as specified by resolution. These water service
charges shall apply to each residential and commercial water service customer
served by the city. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
      2.   Seventy five percent (75%) of an individual water service charge
shall apply to each unit in residential and commercial occupancies classified
as multi-unit. If a single meter serves the multi-unit occupancy, seventy five
percent (75%) of a standard minimum quantity of water will be allowed for each
unit before overage charges are imposed. (Ord. 520, 12-15-2008)
      3.   The city council may, at their discretion, grant water service rate
discounts for residential customers based on age, level of household income, or
both, or other criteria deemed appropriate. Such rate discounts shall apply to
the water base rate and shall not apply to overage consumption rates. Any such
water service rate discount shall be set by resolution. Customers whose service
connection is located outside the city limits shall not be eligible for any
such discount.
      4.   In the event that the water meter for any commercial customer, who
has been determined by the city to be a high consumption water user, cannot be
read due to inaccessibility or nonoperation of the meter, the consumption
portion of the water service charges shall be, whenever possible, an estimation
of a consumption derived from the average of the preceding twelve (12) months'
metered consumption. In instances of estimated billing, all adjustments to any
billing of estimated consumption amounts, due to an estimation greater or
smaller than the actual consumption amount as determined by a meter reading,
shall be made on the first billing following the actual water meter reading.
   B.   Sewer Service:
      1.   There is imposed a monthly sewer base unit charge upon each
residential and commercial base unit receiving sewer service from the city and
shall be as specified by resolution. This sewer base unit charge shall apply to
each residential and commercial sewer service customer.
      2.   The city council may, at their discretion, grant sewer service rate
discounts for residential customers based on age, level of household income, or
both, or other criteria deemed appropriate. Any such sewer service rate
discount shall be set by resolution. Customers whose service connection is
located outside the city limits shall not be eligible for any such discount.
      3.   Based upon an annual consumption audit, or based upon a chemical
analysis of a customer who has been determined by the city by comparison to
industry standards to produce a larger than average quantity of sewer flow, or
a sewage flow proven by chemical analysis to be of a strength or quality that
will put an unusual treatment burden on the wastewater treatment plant, shall
have their base unit charge determined by using a standard equivalent user
formula. Such base unit charges shall become effective thirty (30) days after
official notification of such charges to the customer by the city. (Ord. 482,
6-5-2006)
      4.   Seventy five percent (75%) of a base unit charge shall be charged
for each unit on residential and commercial properties classified as multi-
unit. For commercial properties subject to sewer overage charges, seventy five
percent (75%) of a standard minimum quantity of sewage will be allowed for each
unit before overage charges are imposed. (Ord. 520, 12-15-2008)
      5.   Multi-unit residential and commercial properties shall not have
their base unit charge determined under the large quantity sewer flow generator
provisions as described in subsection B3 of this section.
   C.   Users Outside City Limits Surcharge: There is imposed a surcharge to
the water service charges and sewer base unit charges of customers located
outside the city limits and shall be as specified by resolution. Such surcharge
may, at the discretion of the city council, be waived by the city council for
individual customers. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
   D.   Theft Of Utility Services: The definition and punishment for theft of
utility services shall be as defined and stated in chapter 24 of title 18 of
the Idaho Code. (Ord. 531, 4-19-2010)
8-2-3: FIRE HYDRANT AND TANK TRUCK FILLING CHARGES:
   A.   No person or company shall take city water from any city fire hydrant
without first making application for permission to do so with the city. The
city public works department shall make the determination of fire hydrants
available for usage. Permission to take water from city fire hydrants is hereby
declared surplus usage and is revocable at any time deemed necessary by the
city council.
   B.   No person or company shall connect to a city fire hydrant in such a way
as to pose a threat of backflow into the city water system. All connections to
city fire hydrants shall be protected by an approved backflow prevention method
in compliance with chapter 6 of this title.
   C.   There is imposed a charge for rental and use of a city fire hydrant
meter. The rental charge and the consumption charge shall be as specified by
resolution. There is also imposed a refundable fire hydrant and meter damage
deposit. Such deposit shall be refunded in full upon the return of the fire
hydrant meter in good condition, inspection of the fire hydrant used, for
damage, and upon payment in full of all charges incurred including any damages
to the fire hydrant and meter. Such fire hydrant and meter damage deposit shall
be as specified by resolution. The fire hydrant meter consumption charge shall
be subject to the surcharge imposed in this chapter for usage of fire hydrants
located outside the city limits or for hydrant water used outside the city
limits.
   D.   There is imposed a charge for nonmetered tank truck filling from a city
fire hydrant and shall be as specified by resolution. Nonmetered tank truck
filling will be allowed only for tank trucks of a proven capacity. A tank load
count shall be kept on a tank load tally card supplied by the city. There is
also imposed a refundable fire hydrant damage deposit. Such deposit shall be
refunded in full upon inspection of the fire hydrant used and payment in full
for all water service charges, including fire hydrant damages, incurred. Such
fire hydrant damage deposit shall be as specified in the rate schedule. The
nonmetered tank truck filling charge shall be subject to the surcharge imposed
in this chapter for usage of fire hydrants located outside the city limits or
for hydrant water used outside the city limits.
   E.   The charges and conditions imposed in this section shall not apply to
authorized fire department personnel conducting fire department business.
Violations of this section shall be a misdemeanor. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-2-4: WATER SERVICE TURNON/TURNOFF:
There is imposed a charge for water service turnoff/turnon under the following
specific conditions:
   A.   Emergency Water Service Turnoff/Turnon: There shall be no charge for
one emergency water service turnoff/turnon per calendar year. There is imposed
a charge for all other emergency water service turnoff/turnon per calendar year
and shall be as specified by resolution.
   B.   Seasonal Or Short Term Nonemergency Water Service Turnoff/Turnon: There
is imposed a charge for all seasonal or short term nonemergency water service
turnoff/turnon and shall be as specified by resolution. All such requests for
seasonal or short term nonemergency water service turnoff and turnon shall be
made in writing by the owner. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-2-5: REVIEW OF RATE SCHEDULE:
It shall be the responsibility of the city council to annually review the
current rate schedule to determine the need for any rate adjustments for the
next fiscal year. Such reviews shall be performed during the second regular
city council meeting in July. Adjustments to the rate schedule shall be made by
resolution and shall become effective on October 1 of the year in which the
resolution was passed, or at any time deemed appropriate by the city council.
(Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-2-6: UTILITY IMPROVEMENT BOND ASSESSMENTS:
   A.   Payments for all legally enacted water and/or sewer utility improvement
bonds shall be assessed in accordance with the rate schedule and shall be
charged against all open water and/or sewer utility accounts without regard as
to whether the account is active or inactive. Any utility account that has been
closed at the request of the property owner and reopened in the name of the
same property owner will be assessed for all water and/or sewer utility bond
payments accrued from the date of closing.
   B.   In accordance with USDA loan agreements and conditions, the city shall
not waive utility improvement bond assessments.
   C.   Utility improvement bond assessments are deemed to be a utility service
charge payable in accordance with section
8-1-3 of this title. Delinquent utility improvement bond assessment payments
shall be handled in accordance with section
8-1-4 of this title. (Ord. 536, 7-6-2010, eff. 10-1-2010)
CHAPTER 3
WATER AND SEWER CONNECTION FEES AND CONDITIONS
SECTION:
8-3-1: Water And Sewer Service Connection Applications
8-3-2: Water And Sewer Connection Fees
8-3-3: Responsibility Provisions
8-3-4: Change Of Use
8-3-1: WATER AND SEWER SERVICE CONNECTION APPLICATIONS:
All applications for water and sewer service connections shall be made by the
legal owner of record, or the legal representative of the legal owner of record
(applicant), of the property to be served by the City with a water and sewer
service connection. All applications shall be made on an application for water
and sewer service connection form provided by the City. Such applications may
be presented to the City Council for approval, approval with conditions, or
denial. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-3-2: WATER AND SEWER CONNECTION FEES:
The City shall charge a fee for connection to the City water and sewer systems:
   A.   Basis Of Charges: Water connection fees are based on the water meter
size and are as specified by resolution in the rate schedule. Sewer connection
fees are based on an equivalent residence table adopted by the City Council.
Such table and sewer connection fee shall be specified by resolution in the
rate schedule.
   B.   Transfer Of Service Prohibited: The issuance of water and sewer
connections is the right of the City and the transfer of ownership of a water
and sewer connection to any property, other than to the property it was issued
to, is prohibited. Any such transfer shall become void upon transfer and any
fees paid shall not be refunded.
   C.   Service To Only One Lot: Water and sewer connection fees are based on
one residential or commercial unit per lot. For each additional residential or
commercial unit on a lot serviced by one water and/or sewer connection, a full
water and/or sewer connection fee shall be paid.
   D.   Multiple Connections: For one lot serviced by multiple water and sewer
connections, the fee for each connection shall be as described in the rate
schedule.
   E.   Utility Lines To Front On Property: Water and sewer connection fees are
based on City water and sewer lines fronting an applicant's property. In
instances where the City water and sewer does not front the applicant's
property, and as a condition for City Council approval of an applicant's
request for water and sewer service connection to the City water and sewer main
line, the City water and sewer main lines shall be extended to a point fronting
the applicant's property in a method as described herein.
   F.   Frontage Determination: The determination of whether a City water or
sewer main line fronts an applicant's property shall be made by the City by
extending a point from a property corner bordering a City right-of-way and
closest to a City water or sewer main line that is perpendicular to the
horizontal run of the water or sewer main line. If the end of the City water or
sewer main line lies a minimum of fifteen feet (15') past this extended point,
the City water or sewer main line is considered to front the applicant's
property.
   G.   Impact Mitigation Charges:
      1.   The City shall impose an impact mitigation charge upon any new water
and/or sewer service connection upon determination by the City that the water
and/or sewer connection will have a detrimental effect upon either the water
pressure or flow of the water customers of the contiguous water system or the
adequate sewer flow of the sewer customers of the contiguous sewer system. Such
impact mitigation fee shall be determined by the City and shall be based upon
the estimated cost of mitigating any such proven detrimental effects to the
contiguous water and/or sewer system that are attributable to the new
connection. In areas where future water and/or sewer connections are possible,
such impact mitigation fees shall be determined on a pro rata basis based upon
the estimated number of possible future water and/or sewer connections.
      2.   The City shall impose an impact mitigation charge upon any new water
and/or sewer service connection upon determination by the City that the water
and/or sewer connection will have a detrimental effect on the City's ability to
properly operate and maintain the City water and/or sewer system in its
entirety. Such impact mitigation fee shall be determined by the City and shall
be based upon the estimated cost of mitigating any such detrimental effect on
City's ability to properly operate and maintain the City water and/or sewer
system in its entirety.
   H.   Fee Payments: All water and sewer connection fees, and impact
mitigation charges shall be due and payable at the time of issuance of a
building permit for the applicable lot. The collection of water and/or sewer
fees prior to the issuance of a building permit, hereinafter referred to as
prepaid connection fees, shall be discouraged by the City Council but may be
collected upon exception granted by the City Council. Under no circumstances
shall impact mitigation charges be collected prior to the issuance of a
building permit. If any water and/or sewer connection is deemed an abandoned
connection, as defined in this chapter, said connection shall be only
reinstated after compliance with section
8-3-1 of this chapter and payment of the required connection fee.
   I.   Fire Service Connections: All commercial occupancies required to
provide fire protection systems shall be required to install a separate fire
service connection to the City water system. Such fire service connection shall
be sized according to required fire flow and shall be installed in accordance
with chapter 7, "Water And Sewer System Construction Standards", of this title
and shall provide for backflow prevention in accordance with chapter 6,
"Backflow Prevention And Cross Connection Control", of this title. All fire
service connections, two inches (2") or larger in size, shall be equipped with
fire flow detector assemblies. The connection fee for a fire service connection
shall be specified by resolution in the rate schedule.
   J.   Abandoned Connection: All water and/or sewer connections that have been
abandoned or have not been used for thirty six (36) consecutive months or that
for any reason have become useless for further service shall be deemed an
abandoned connection. Any abandoned connection shall be disconnected at the
main by the property owner or the Public Works Department, and all pipe and
appurtenances removed shall be the property of the City. (Ord. 603, 4-15-2019)
8-3-3: RESPONSIBILITY PROVISIONS:
   A.   Water And Sewer Main Line Extensions:
      1.   All water and sewer main line extensions required to serve any new
subdivision (as defined in the existing City Subdivision Ordinance) with water
and sewer service shall be done in compliance with the current City Subdivision
Ordinance.
      2.   Water and sewer main line extensions for water or sewer service
connection applicants, whose property is located in a previously platted
subdivision within the City limits, shall be made at the expense of the City;
providing that the subdivision was under the jurisdiction of the City at the
time the plat was recorded; and providing that the subdivision was required to
install water and sewer main lines as a condition to platting the subdivision
under the then existing Subdivision Ordinance; and providing the City Council
approves the applicant's request for water and sewer service connection; and
providing that the applicant's property was not created in a manner that could
be classified as a subdivision as defined in the existing City Subdivision
Ordinance, in which instances responsibility for extension of City water and
sewer main line shall be done in compliance with the current City Subdivision
Ordinance.
      3.   For water and sewer service connection applicants whose property is
not located in a previously platted subdivision, and which requires an
extension of the City water and sewer main lines to service the property, the
responsibility for such extensions in a method as described herein shall be the
applicant's.
   B.   Connections And Maintenance:
      1.   The City may, upon payment of a water service installation fee,
provide all materials and labor to effect a water service connection to the
applicant's closest property or easement line, providing the applicant's
property meets the conditions described herein. This connection shall include
the City water main tap, piping, meter and meter box, and for all trenching,
backfilling and compaction required to effect the installation; except that it
shall not include any costs associated with asphalt pavement repair and
replacement, which shall be the responsibility of the applicant and shall be
charged in addition to the water service installation fee upon completion of
the pavement repair. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
      2.   It is the responsibility of the City to maintain and repair the
water service line from the City main water line to the property line dividing
the applicant's property, or easement, and the City right-of-way. It is also
the responsibility of the City to maintain and repair the City water meter,
regardless of the location of the water meter, and the associated meter setting
appurtenances. It shall not be the responsibility of the City to maintain any
water service line that lies upon or within private property. (Ord. 538, 1-3-
2011)
      3.   It is the responsibility of the applicant to furnish all materials
and labor to extend a sewer service lateral line from the City sewer main line
to the applicant's property or easement line, except that the City may furnish
the sewer tapping saddle. Such service line shall also include the installation
of a sewer backflow device if it is determined that the lowest plumbing fixture
drain in the dwelling is lower than the manhole rim elevation of the nearest
downstream or upstream manhole serving the dwelling. The cost of such
installation shall be the responsibility of the property owner.
      4.   It shall also be the responsibility of the owner to maintain the
sewer service lateral line from the City sewer main line to the owner's
property line, or easement line, dividing the owner's property, or easement,
and the City right-of-way, and responsibility for maintenance shall include the
tap into the City sewer main line. When existing sewer lateral lines are
retrofitted with a sewer backflow device, the City shall supply the device and
associated parts and shall reimburse the property owner an amount specified by
the Council in the rate resolution for the installation of such device. (Ord.
509, 3-17-2008)
      5.   All water and sewer service connections shall be made in compliance
with sections
8-7-3 and
8-7-4 of this title.
   C.   Water And Sewer Connection Size: It shall be the responsibility of the
City to determine the required size of the water and sewer service connections
and shall be based on flow requirements as submitted by the applicant. (Ord.
482, 6-5-2006)
8-3-4: CHANGE OF USE:
Total water and sewer service connection fees are determined utilizing: a) the
equivalent residential unit (ERU) table and b) the current water and sewer
connection fee table, both of which are contained in the current rate
resolution. If a change of use is requested that would materially increase the
number of ERUs determined under a previous use, the City shall recalculate the
ERUs and determine whether additional water and/or sewer connection fees are
applicable. The property owner will be given credit for any ERU determination
used in the original connection fee determination. Any additional connection
fees shall be based upon the water and/or sewer connection fee schedule in
effect at the time of the ERU redetermination. In no instance shall the City
rebate any connection fees paid by any owner of the property. (Ord. 524, 6-1-
2009)
CHAPTER 4
WATER SYSTEM REGULATIONS
SECTION:
8-4-1: Water Use Authority
8-4-2: Right Of Entry
8-4-3: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
8-4-1: WATER USE AUTHORITY:
   A.   In the interest of public health and safety, the city council is
authorized to regulate the water usage drawn from the city water system and may
pass such ordinances, resolutions and regulations as it may deem necessary to
protect the city water supply and control water usage.
   B.   Notices of any such ordinances, resolutions and regulations pertaining
to the protection and control of city water shall be given by publication in
the official newspaper of the city, and such ordinances, resolutions and
regulations shall become effective on the date of such publication and notice.
   C.   At any time deemed necessary by the city council, water usage not
necessary for potable or fire protection use may be declared surplus usage and
its discontinuance so ordered by the city council. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-4-2: RIGHT OF ENTRY:
All persons or companies receiving water from the city water system shall be
required to admit, upon reasonable notice if such notice is so requested,
properly identified city employees onto their property for purposes of water
meter reading and discontinuance of city water service. Refusal to grant entry
shall result in the immediate discontinuance of city water service. (Ord. 482,
6-5-2006)
8-4-3: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
Violations of the provisions of this section shall be considered misdemeanors:
   A.   Unauthorized Supplying Of Water: It is unlawful for any person or
company legally receiving water from the city water system at any residence or
place of business to supply water from said source to any other residence or
place of business without first obtaining the written approval of the city.
   B.   Unauthorized Taking Of City Water: It is unlawful for any person or
company to take water from the city water system without first making
application to the city.
   C.   Meter Tampering: It is unlawful for any person or company to cause to
be disconnected, circumvented, readjusted, or otherwise tampered with, any city
water meter or water meter setting equipment. For the purposes of this
subsection, any valve controlling the flow of water into the meter shall be
considered as part of the meter setting equipment. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
CHAPTER 5
SEWER SYSTEM REGULATIONS
SECTION:
8-5-1: Enforcement Policy
8-5-2: Connection To Sewer System Required
8-5-3: Private Sewage Disposal Systems
8-5-4: Maintenance Responsibility
8-5-5: Commercial And Industrial Wastewater Pretreatment Program
8-5-6: Sand And Grease Interceptors
8-5-7: Public Utility Access
8-5-8: Prohibited Discharges
8-5-9: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
8-5-1: ENFORCEMENT POLICY:
It is declared the policy of the city that enforcement of the provisions of
this chapter shall be by discontinuation of city water service, or by penalties
as described, or both. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-5-2: CONNECTION TO SEWER SYSTEM REQUIRED:
Owners of all houses, buildings or properties used for human occupancy,
employment, recreation or other purposes located within the jurisdiction of the
city and abutting any street, alleyway or city right of way in which there is
located a public sanitary sewer of the city sewer system, are required at their
expense to install suitable toilet facilities therein, and to connect such
facilities directly with the city sewer within ninety (90) days after official
notice by the city to do so, provided that such public sewer is within three
hundred feet (300') of the closest property line. Where sewer connections are
made as provided herein, septic tanks, cesspools and drywells and all other
private sewage disposal systems shall be physically bypassed and permanently
disconnected from sewer lines and their use permanently abandoned. Such
facilities shall be filled and compacted. A violation of this section shall be
a misdemeanor. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-5-3: PRIVATE SEWAGE DISPOSAL SYSTEMS:
Violations of the provisions of this section shall be considered misdemeanors:
   A.   Properties within the jurisdiction of the city that do not have a city
sewer located within three hundred feet (300') of their closest property line
may, with the approval of the city and the local health district, construct
such private sewage disposal systems as approved by the city and the local
health district.
   B.   Properties located within three hundred feet (300') of a city sewer and
served by a private sewage disposal system are required to connect to the city
sewer within six (6) months, except that the city council may grant a time
extension to this requirement. Such time extension shall expire when it is
determined by the city or the local health district that the private sewage
disposal system will no longer function without repairs that would require the
issuance of a permit from the local health district.
   C.   Except as provided for in this chapter, it is unlawful to construct or
maintain any private sewage disposal system intended for, or used for, the
disposal of sewage. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-5-4: MAINTENANCE RESPONSIBILITY:
A sewer lateral, which shall be an extension from the owner's building sewer
drain to the city sewer, including the sewer main line tap, shall be owned and
maintained by the owner of the premises upon which the building is located, and
the city shall not be responsible in any manner for its maintenance or repair.
(Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-5-5: COMMERCIAL AND INDUSTRIAL WASTEWATER PRETREATMENT PROGRAM:
   A.   It is declared the policy of the city that commercial and industrial
sewage flow into the city sewer be controlled and monitored in conformance with
the provisions of this chapter. As such, development and enforcement of a
commercial/industrial wastewater pretreatment program is a necessary means to
control sewage waste discharged into the city sewer by commercial and
industrial sewer users.
   B.   The city council shall, if deemed necessary, appoint a pretreatment
program administrator to develop and administer a commercial/industrial
wastewater pretreatment program, the purpose of which shall be the enforcement
of the provisions of this chapter concerning commercial and industrial wastes.
   C.   The administrator shall have the powers and duties to: develop and
administer the program within the provisions of this chapter; make
determinations of sewage flows from commercial and industrial dischargers; make
determinations of the type of pretreatment required; require the installation
of any pretreatment equipment determined to be needed; require the periodic
testing and maintenance of pretreatment equipment; recommend to the city
council the discontinuance of water service to any customer who fails to comply
with the provisions of this chapter; and keep all appropriate records regarding
the administration of the program. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-5-6: SAND AND GREASE INTERCEPTORS:
   A.   Grease, oil and sand separators shall be provided when, in the opinion
of the administrator, they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid
wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand
and other harmful ingredients; except that such interceptors shall not be
required for private living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall
be of a type and capacity approved by the administrator, and shall be located
as to be readily and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection.
   B.   Grease, oil and sand separators shall be constructed of impervious
materials and shall be designed to be capable of withstanding abrupt and
extreme changes in temperature. Separators shall be of substantial construction
and designed for the type of traffic they will be subject to; shall be
watertight, and equipped with easily removable covers which, when bolted in
place, shall be gastight.
   C.   Where installed, all grease, oil and sand separators shall be
maintained by the owner, at their expense, in continuously efficient operation
at all times.
   D.   A violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor. In addition,
violators shall pay for costs of remediation of damages caused by a violation
of this section. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-5-7: PUBLIC UTILITY ACCESS:
   A.   When, in the opinion of the administrator, because of the quantity or
the chemical quality of the discharge, a customer's discharge into the city
sewer has a potential to disrupt the bacteriological functioning of the
wastewater treatment plant, or poses a potential danger to the wastewater
treatment plant, or to the plant personnel, or to the city sewer, the
administrator may require, as a provision of the program, the installation of a
monitoring manhole in the customer's sewer lateral line, to be located on the
customer's premises, downstream of the last customer inlet into their sewer
lateral line, and before the connection into the city sewer, the purpose of
which is to allow the city to monitor and sample the customer's discharge into
the city sewer.
   B.   When required in accordance with this section, a monitoring manhole
shall be installed as directed by the administrator. The customer shall be
responsible for the costs of installation of the monitoring manhole, and shall
maintain the monitoring manhole at all times so as to provide a safe entry and
exit.
   C.   When required in accordance with this section, a monitoring manhole
shall be installed in such a way as to provide access to authorized city
personnel at all times in order to effect measurements and sampling of the
customer's discharge into the city sewer.
   D.   A violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor. In addition,
violators shall pay for costs incurred by the city for installation of a
monitoring manhole as required in accordance with this section. (Ord. 482, 6-5-
2006)
8-5-8: PROHIBITED DISCHARGES:
   A.   Except as provided for in this chapter, no person or company shall
discharge, or cause to be discharged, any of the following described waters or
wastes to the city sewer:
      1.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F);
      2.   Any fat, oil, grease, gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil, or other
flammable or explosive liquid, solid or gas;
      3.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded;
      4.   Any ashes, cinders, mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags,
feathers, tar, plastic, wood, paunch manure, or any other solid or viscous
substance capable of causing obstruction to the flow in sewers, or other
interference with the proper operation of the wastewater treatment facility;
      5.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or higher than 9.0,
or having any corrosive properties capable of causing damage or hazard to
structures, equipment or personnel of the wastewater treatment facility;
      6.   Any waters or wastes containing a toxic or poisonous substance in
sufficient quantity to injure or interfere with any wastewater treatment
process, constitute a hazard to humans or animals or create a hazard in the
receiving waters of the wastewater treatment facility;
      7.   Any waters or wastes containing suspended solids of such character
and quantity that unusual attention or expense is required to handle such
materials at the wastewater treatment facility;
      8.   Any noxious or malodorous gas or substance capable of creating a
public nuisance;
      9.   Any milk product wastes;
      10.   Any liquid or solid that may cause, because of its chemical
composition, strength, toxicity, or volume, the wastewater treatment facility
to violate the city's national pollutant discharge elimination system (NPDES)
discharge permit conditions or limitations, or that may affect the city's
ultimate disposal of sewage waste;
      11.   Any solid or liquid that would have an adverse effect on the city
sewer, or any portion thereof.
   B.   All commercial and industrial users of the city sewer shall be subject
to pretreatment inspection and shall be subject to the terms and conditions of
the commercial/industrial wastewater pretreatment monitoring program.
   C.   A violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor. In addition,
violators shall pay all costs incurred by the city for investigations, testing,
fines or penalties paid by the city to other governmental agencies or private
parties due to a violation of this section, and for the costs of remedial
actions taken by and for the city for damages caused by a violation of this
section. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-5-9: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Discharge Of Stormwater And Other Unpolluted Waters To City Sewers: No
person or company shall discharge, or cause to be discharged, any stormwater,
surface water, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, floor drainage,
cooling water or polluted or unpolluted industrial process waters to the city
sewer. A violation of this subsection shall be a misdemeanor. In addition,
violators shall pay for costs of remediation of damages caused by a violation
of this section.
   B.   Sewage Or Waste Deposits: It is unlawful for any person or company to
place or deposit, or permit to be placed or deposited, in any unsanitary manner
upon any public or private property within the city, or in any area under the
jurisdiction of the city, any human or animal excrement, garbage or other
objectionable waste. A violation of this subsection shall be a misdemeanor and,
upon conviction, violators shall pay all costs incurred by the city for
prosecution of a violation of this subsection, and for costs of remediation of
damages caused by a violation of this subsection.
   C.   Discharging Sewage Or Polluted Waters In Natural Outlets: It is
unlawful to discharge to any natural outlet within the city, or in any area
under the jurisdiction of the city, any sanitary sewage, industrial waste or
other polluted waters, except where suitable treatment has been provided in
accordance with the provisions of this chapter. A violation of this subsection
shall be a misdemeanor. In addition, violators shall pay all costs incurred by
the city for investigations, testing, fines or penalties paid by the city to
other governmental agencies or private parties due to a violation of this
subsection, and for the costs of remedial actions taken by and for the city for
damages caused by a violation of this subsection.
   D.   Tampering Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person, company or
corporation, without authority from the public works supervisor, to open any
sewer manhole or interfere with or tamper with, in any manner, any sewer
manhole or city sewer. A violation of this subsection shall be a misdemeanor.
In addition, violators shall pay for costs of remediation of damages caused by
a violation of this subsection. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
CHAPTER 6
BACKFLOW PREVENTION AND CROSS CONNECTION CONTROL
SECTION:
8-6-1: Purpose
8-6-2: Administration And Program
8-6-3: Rules And Regulations
8-6-4: Right Of Entry
8-6-5: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
8-6-6: Remedies
8-6-1: PURPOSE:
Pursuant to the Idaho administrative procedures act (IDAPA) 16.01.08550.06, it
is the responsibility of the city to protect the city water system from
contamination due to backflow. The purpose of this chapter is to guard the
public health and safety of the water consumer by enforcement of the provisions
of this chapter. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-6-2: ADMINISTRATION AND PROGRAM:
   A.   The mayor shall, with the approval of the city council, appoint a cross
connection control administrator to develop and administer a backflow
prevention and cross connection control program for the purpose of
administering the provisions of this chapter.
   B.   In the interest of the public health and safety, and as a means for the
city and administrator to develop and administer the backflow prevention and
cross connection control program, the "Cross Connection Control Manual -
Accepted Procedure And Practice", latest edition, as published by the cross
connection control committee, Pacific Northwest section, American Waterworks
Association, and as the same may be revised by the publishing authority, and
the same is hereby adopted and incorporated as part of this chapter as fully as
though set forth at length in this chapter.
   C.   The administrator shall have the powers and duties to: develop and
administer the program within the guidelines of the IDAPA and the Idaho
department of environmental quality (DEQ); make determinations of the existence
of cross connections and the level of backflow protection required; require the
discontinuance of cross connections; require the installation of backflow
prevention assemblies; direct the discontinuance of water service to any
customer who fails to comply with this chapter; require the periodic testing
and maintenance of backflow prevention assemblies; keep all appropriate records
regarding the administration of the program; and, recommend to the city council
any changes required to the program or this chapter. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-6-3: RULES AND REGULATIONS:
   A.   City Authority: The city shall make or prescribe such rules and
regulations as it shall deem advisable for the implementation and enforcement
of the provisions of this chapter. Such rules and regulations shall be in
accordance with the guidelines of the DEQ.
   B.   General Regulations:
      1.   Backflow And Cross Connection Prohibited: The installation or
maintaining of any backflow or cross connection, actual or potential, is
prohibited. Any such backflow or cross connection now existing is declared
unlawful and shall be eliminated immediately. A violation of this subsection
shall be a misdemeanor. A violator shall also be subject to immediate
discontinuance of water service.
      2.   Backflow Prevention And Cross Connection Control Required: When, in
the determination of the administrator, there exists a need for backflow
prevention and/or cross connection control, the city water supplied to any
customer shall be contingent upon the customer providing backflow prevention
and/or cross connection control in a manner approved by the administrator and
the DEQ.
      3.   Backflow Prevention Assembly Approval:
         a.   Any backflow prevention assembly required by the administrator to
be installed shall be a type approved for the specific degree of hazard it will
be used for, by the University of Southern California Foundation for Cross
Connection Control and Hydraulic Research (USC-FCCCHR) and shall be installed
in accordance with the manual.
         b.   All backflow prevention assemblies shall be tested a minimum of
once a year by a tester approved by the administrator. A copy of all test
results and any repairs required shall be delivered to the administrator. All
required testing and repairs shall be done at the expense of the customer.
         c.   The customer shall have full responsibility to maintain any
required backflow prevention assembly in proper operating order. (Ord. 482, 6-
5-2006)
      4.   Fire Protection System Backflow Preventers: All commercial fire
protection systems, two inches (2") in size and larger, served by the city
shall be equipped with an approved detector double check valve backflow
prevention assembly (hereinafter "detector check assembly"). Such detector
check assembly shall be equipped with a bypass water meter that shall
accurately detect flows through the detector check assembly and such bypass
meter shall be equipped with a separate double check valve assembly. Detector
check assemblies shall be installed and maintained in compliance with the
manual. (Ord. 525, 7-20-2009)
8-6-4: RIGHT OF ENTRY:
All persons or companies receiving water from the city water system shall be
required to admit, upon reasonable notice if such notice be so requested, city
employees onto their property for purposes of inspecting for cross connections
and ascertaining the proper operation of backflow prevention assemblies.
Refusal to grant entry shall result in the immediate discontinuation of water
service. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-6-5: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
   A.   Tampering: It is unlawful for any person or company to cause to be
disconnected, circumvented, readjusted or otherwise tampered with any backflow
prevention device, except for a person approved by the administrator for
testing and repairing such devices. A violation of this subsection shall be a
misdemeanor. In addition, a violator shall pay all costs incurred by the city
for remediation of damages caused by a violation of this section.
   B.   Failure To Comply: For failure to comply with the terms of this
chapter, or any part thereof, the city shall have the right, in order to
protect the health and safety of the public, to take all actions necessary,
including prosecution of violations of this chapter and discontinuation of
water service to any customer. Such discontinuation shall continue until such
time as the administrator finds the customer in compliance with this chapter.
Any and all costs incurred by the city in obtaining customer compliance shall
be the responsibility of the customer and shall be reimbursed by the customer
to the city before compliance is certified and water service is restored. (Ord.
482, 6-5-2006)
8-6-6: REMEDIES:
It is declared the policy of the city that enforcement of the provisions of
this chapter shall be by discontinuation of city water service, or by penalties
as described, or both. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
CHAPTER 7
WATER AND SEWER SYSTEM CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS
SECTION:
8-7-1: Public Works Inspector
8-7-2: Idaho Standards For Public Works Construction
8-7-3: Water System Construction Standards
8-7-4: Sewer System Construction Standards
8-7-5: Public Utility Installation Bonding, Licensing And Insurance
8-7-1: PUBLIC WORKS INSPECTOR:
   A.   Appointment: The mayor shall, with the approval of the city council,
appoint a public works employee as the city public works inspector.
   B.   Powers And Duties: The city public works inspector shall, under the
direction of the mayor and city council, ensure compliance of all public works
projects with all applicable codes, laws, standards and ordinances and shall
keep accurate records and maps of all public works construction, and shall
periodically review all applicable standards and ordinances to ensure
compliance with federal and state statutes. Under the direction of the mayor
and city council, the public works inspector shall have the power to take any
legal actions necessary, up to and including stopping works in progress, to
ensure compliance with all applicable codes, laws, standards and ordinances.
(Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-7-2: IDAHO STANDARDS FOR PUBLIC WORKS CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Purpose: It is declared the policy of the city that public utility
systems be constructed and installed in a uniform manner, consistent with
accepted construction practices, for the protection of the water and sewer
system users. Toward that end, adoption of the latest edition of the Idaho
standards for public works construction, as amended by the city council, is a
necessary means of assuring consistency and uniformity of the construction and
installation of public utility systems and services within the jurisdiction of
the city.
   B.   Standards Adopted By Reference: There is adopted, for the purpose of
establishing rules and regulations for the construction and installation of
public utility systems and services, those certain standards identified as the
"Idaho Standards For Public Work Construction (ISPWC)", latest edition, as
published by the Idaho standards for public works construction committee and as
amended by the city council as the same may be revised by the publishing
authority, or as amended by the city council, and the same is adopted and
incorporated as part of this chapter as fully as though set forth at length
herein. One copy of the latest edition of said standards, as amended by the
city council, shall be kept on file with the city. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-7-3: WATER SYSTEM CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS:
   A.   Specifications For Water System Construction:
      1.   All water systems, or part thereof, constructed and installed within
the city, shall be constructed and installed in compliance with the ISPWC as
adopted by the city council in section
8-7-2 of this chapter.
      2.   All water system construction plans shall be reviewed and approved
by the Idaho department of environmental quality prior to installation.
      3.   All materials used in the construction of a water system shall be
inspected and approved by the public works inspector prior to installation and
shall be installed in accordance with manufacturer's instructions.
      4.   All parts of a constructed and installed water system shall be
inspected and approved by the public works inspector and/or the engineer's
inspector prior to backfilling.
      5.   Strict compliance with all federal and state safety rules,
regulations and standards regarding trenching, traffic control and work zone
safety shall be enforced by the public works inspector. Failure to comply with
the provisions of this subsection shall result in work stoppage.
   B.   Prohibited Acts:
      1.   Unauthorized Connection To City Water System: It is unlawful to
connect to, or cause to be connected to, the city water system any other water
system, or part thereof, without the approval of the city.
      2.   Tampering With City Water System Prohibited: It is unlawful for any
person to tamper with, or cause to be tampered with, the city water system, or
any part thereof.
   C.   Violation: A violation of this section shall be a misdemeanor. In
addition, violators shall pay all costs incurred by the city for all remedial
actions taken by the city to repair damages caused by a violation of this
section. (Ord. 482, 6-5-2006)
8-7-4: SEWER SYSTEM CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS:
   A.   Specifications For Sewer System Construction:
      1.   All sewer systems, or part thereof, constructed and installed within
the city, shall be constructed and installed in compliance with the ISPWC as
adopted by the city council in section
8-7-2 of this chapter.
      2.   Prior to installation, all sewer system construction plans shall be
reviewed and approved by the Idaho department of environmental quality.
      3.   All materials used in the construction of a sewer system shall be
inspected and approved by the public works inspector prior to installation and
shall be installed in accordance with the manufacturer's instructions.
      4.   All parts of a constructed and installed sewer system shall be
inspected and approved by the public works inspector and/or the engineer's
inspector prior to backfilling.
      5.   Strict compliance with all federal and state safety rules,
regulations and standards regarding trenching, traffic control and work zone
safety shall be enforced by the public works inspector. Failure to comply with
the provisions of this subsection shall result in work stoppage.
   B.   Prohibited Acts:
      1.   Unauthorized Connections: It is unlawful to connect to, or cause to
be connected to, the city sewer system, or any other sewer system, or part
thereof, without the approval of the city.
